申報本埠增刊

談言

富翁厭棄阿堵物

— 柳

咱們中國在古昔的時候，曾經有過一個文人對於金錢厭惡之至，呌金錢不呌金錢而呼曰阿堵物，卽是厭惡這種東西連它的名字都厭惡者也。可是，這文人並非富翁，他厭惡金錢的原因，大槪是因為缺乏金錢，受了金錢的壓迫而厭惡金錢，這在金錢世界的現社會上，並不為奇。報載希臘的雅典有一個大富翁大實業家名呌賴麻氏者，特發怪癖，在他的住宅的樓頭，以一百五百及一千特拉格曼（希臘幣名）的鈔票向下散播。給過往的路人爭相搶取。在這全世界經濟恐慌，富者益富貴者益貧的矛盾社會，窮人之對於金錢，心裏固然厭惡眼裏却是發亮，也難怪雅典的窮人聽到富翁散播鈔票不約而集者千萬人，爭相搶取空中飛舞的鈔票，以至「爭呶化為暴亂。」

富翁因為拚命攫有了金錢然後才成為其富翁，現在這洋富翁却說是他對於這種齷齪錢財深惡痛絕，並且說是他深受阿堵物之累，感覺厭倦，這也就足以知道金錢這種東西給人厭惡無論貧富了。　　考上古之時，貿易之道只是以物易物，後來不知是誰却發明以錢幣作中間流通的法寳，自從社會上有了這種法寳以來，本是人用法寳，其後却是法寳用人了，這發明家說亦可惡之至。我國歷史稗傳以及傳說神話對於發明火者說是燧人氏，對於發明醫藥者說是神農氏，對於發明航海的羅盤指南針者。說是黄帝，可是對於這錢幣的發明家，却是並無明文紀載，大槪「始作俑者其無後乎」，他連名字都没世而名不宣了。這錢幣發明家之所以没世而名不宣的原因，又可以說是古之人也深惡痛絕於金錢，不願有如宣揚燧人氏神農氏的盛德一樣將他的大名流傳後世了。

春秋之世，孔子曰「富而可求，雖執鞭之士吾亦為之，」足見在那時已經有了富人，而且在那時的富人已經了不得，所以孔子雖然不願求富，但亦教子貢以貨殖之道。不過聖人如孔子者尙且只是不願求富而並不對於金錢深惡痛絕，可見金錢的魔力聖人亦莫如之何。現在這希臘國裏的洋富翁竟是厭惡起金錢來，難道他比較咱們中國的聖人還了不得？

報載後來警士以他是「神經錯亂，卽送入某醫院，」這在資本社會的國家要維持資本制度的尊嚴，自然以他是「神經錯亂」最為良法，可是再不能够聽到這一位厭棄金錢的富翁的言論實在可惜。

在上海的富翁們，並没有聽見他們對於金錢厭棄，其實一成為富翁，便有被綁票匪綁架勒索之虞，行動不自由，提心吊膽，明明是受了金錢之累，他們怎麼甘願如此？這所以金錢制度是特别偉大的原因吧？可是，在窮人看來，這一種金錢制度，卽是造成萬惡社會的泉源總機關，誰都在咒詛誰都在深惡痛絕，此所以社會就不會安寗的原因吧？　　假如全世界的富翁都厭棄金錢，天下一定太平，我作如是想。

减租運動

— 光漢

近日本巿各團體因　於淞滬戰後，巿面狀况，日益蕭條，而各處房租，非但未見减輕，甚有還在增加，多要求减低房租，以輕負但，而復興巿廛繁榮計，特組一委員會，作减租運動之舉，這是件値得我人注意的事。

人生問題，切要者除衣食而外，當然要算是住了。上海為我國通商大埠，全巿人口，已達三百餘萬之多，是住的問題，已成為社會上一個嚴重的問題。自來上海房租之昂貴，本為全國各地冠，而一般擁有房產者，又每只知自肥，不顧民生，時有加租之舉，到無數居民，終年血汗所得，幾大半盡輸於房東。影響所及，個人生計的感受困迫，自不待言，巿面亦將因之而衰敗，社會亦必隨之而呈不安之象。補救之道，捨减租外，别無良策。故减租運動，實為今日解决居民居住問題應有的正當行為。蓋解决居住問題，不僅可以使個人能得安居樂業、同時亦足以促進巿塲的繁興，維持社會的寗靜。　　但我人對於該運動，雖一面表示十分贊助之忱，一面尙不免覺有一大缺陷。卽該會所欲致力者，似乎只在代表各商舖及各二房東對大房東的一種减租的要求，而於三房客，則蓋置諸腦後。這從該會的議决案可以看出。　　於此，我人要問一問，一法的居民，租屋居住者，商舖及二房東外，不是尙有所謂三房客嗎？全巿三房客究有多少，雖没有統計，爲數之衆，當可斷言。而且二房東又常將白已所遭大房東的壓迫，轉加諸三房客的身上，是則三房客所受的痛苦，亦不亞於二房東。今二房東旣不願忍受大房東的盤剝，起而作减租之要求，實爲情勢所使然。而三房客不也是一樣有充分的理由以反抗二房東的榨取的嗎，故我以爲該會如果僅僅是代表二房東說話，那末這種運動，還是不澈底的運動，於全體的居民，亦是没有多大影響的。或許有人說，大房東的房租一减低，不但二房東直接受其賜，卽三房客亦間接沾其利了。蓋二房東所要求的目的一達到，對於三房家的租金，自然也就可以减輕了。我想這話也未必盡是。須知人類的本性是自私的，二房東雖然自身覺得痛楚，向大房東去呼籲，但他們對於三房客的境遇，也不一定就會同情，就肯退讓。故我以爲社會人士如果眞有心要解蘇民困，復興巿面，維護社會，這個减租運動，該須澈底而且普遍，不惟對大房東應作减租的要求，卽對二房東，亦須作同樣的勸吿。這樣於上海大多數的住民，才是有益，而於巿塲的繁榮，社會的安寗，亦才有所補救！

理想生活的自白

— 文炳

一般人一提起做人，便好像非削尖頭皮鑽入這惡濁的社會不可似的，可是，我却最恨這種論調。我總覺得這是種奴性的發揮，是種人的卑劣行爲最刻骨的暴露。爲什麼做人一定要奴顏婢膝呢？爲什麼做人定要去仰承那般污濁者流的鼻息，而苟且偸生？這種人性的乖離，我是不解的。我不解爲甚麼他們一定要鑽進這所謂職業的社會，而互相排擠着，傾軋着，把人家打倒自已却飛奔上去代替他？爲什麼他們定要這樣的卑劣呢？假使人類的生命是要以這樣卑劣的行爲去替它着色的，那他們爲什麼不遽然地死去？

在我，我是與他們叛離的。我不能有他們這種存心。假使我要有這種存心　　那麼我早已非我。而早是他們中的一員了。

在我，雖然一樣的覺得生來了就只得願存的生，但我却没有他們那樣去生的意見；要是我去奴顏婢膝，仰承人家鼻息的生，那我最好早就死去。因爲所謂生，就要有種高貴的意義，一種生命意識的活躍，是無論怎樣都不會在這種奴顏婢膝上表現它的尊貴的。

我將怎樣擇取生活的方式呢？我，認定是要這樣的：我將决計像那些昔賢似的過着隱士生活，我寗願淡泊，寗願在羣山萬壑中隱棲着而寂然無聞。我不去拜訪甚麼偉人，也不親近什麼權貴。讓自然永是醇然而聖潔地臨着我，讓明月爲我作伴，讓清泉爲我照心！讓那社會的制裁，社會的束縛永遠的離開我。

從這種清靜的生活裏，讓我沉浸在那般古代詩人的詩靈中，讓我這顆不被勢利薰染着的心，永遠和這般偉大的聖潔的心同在着。至於世界，我願拋棄給那般勢利之徒，讓他們在會訪中以炸彈手槍相見吧！讓他們朋友陷害着朋友，親人陷害着親人！………

也許有人要駡我在信口雌黄，但這正是他錯了！在這種污濁而無法挿足的社會裏，能够從一切紛爭中㧞足跑出來，不但不傲岸旁觀，而且率然的隱去，這不能不說是另有一種自然的心境吧！難道這樣一點都不擾攘人家，一點都不干預人家的生活也是世人所不許的麼？要是連這點也不要，那這眞是暴世了！「夫復何言」！

愛情商品化的必然性

— 列火

一般人（也許我亦在內）每每痛絕現代女人的愛情被金錢蹂躪了，簡直成了商品，話雖不錯，其實乃是事實所必然，這世界有什麼東西不被金錢蹂躪呢？更有那一種東西不成了商品呢？辛克萊的屠塲裏，關於殺牛塲的情形，曾有過這樣的描寫，他說因爲機器的組織嚴密，不論是牛肉，牛皮，牛骨，牛毛都不會任意的蹧蹋半點，就是牛血，牛糞也都各有它的用處；唯一不能使它成爲商品的，祇是牛被殺葉，那慘痛的呼聲。這當然是種刻　的描寫，也是種眞實的描寫，因爲現社會的精神就是如此。

假使我們知道現社會不但是體力勞動成爲商品，並且就是智力勞動也使之成爲商品之後，我們對於現社會之使愛

Page 23

情成為商品，也將不會驚奇了。工人要生活他們便出賣他們的勞動力。智識分子如學者，教授，哲學家，文學家，藝術家，科學家等，　為要生活，他們便出賣着智識，著作，藝術品，新發明。而一個女人為要使她自已生存，在她没有比肉體比愛情更好的東西去出賣的時候，她便祇得將她的唯一的肉體愛情出賣給那買者了。這其間為的是生存問題，假使一個人能够體念得求生的那種熱切的要求，他對於這種為生存而出賣着自已最實貴的東西，也將會無怪其然了。一個現代的女子本來是難得謀生的，假使我們注意到她們的才能，她們的體質，她們的地位，必能了解這點。就是她們和男子們站在一個平等的地位，也是難得戰勝男子，何况她們是處在一種比男子不同的地位？我們知道，凡是人都是要生存的，女人當然不會例外。可是她們憑藉什麼去生存呢？這里便是她們出賣愛情的最大理由。她們是動人的，是騒蕩的，這動人和騒蕩的兩大原素便構成了她們成為商品的主要成分。加以，她們是特别喜歡虛榮，而虛榮的表現又都是些要用許多金錢才可以購得來的什物。於是她們的當然購買者，也當然是那些有錢的，能够常常買這些高貴的什物來滿足她們的虛榮的購買者了。

照一般的說來，祇有動人的儀容，青年的英俊，一種殷勤的熱烈的心情，才是引起女人發生愛情的原素，本來這是對的。不過這些東西到底不是金錢，在她們想，那管是一個非常英俊可愛的青年，假使祇能在一間低矮的穢臭的草棚中去安置着他的愛人，這將會是一件多麼痛心的事。所以在我們看來，靈榮彷彿是不重要，然而這在女人凑不能這樣想。在封建社會里，人的高低是以爵位來表現的，那時是有窮得不名一文的貴族受人敬重，高貴的宴會上常有穿着破綻的貴族服的事實。這種，那管窮得没有一文錢，穿着破衣也還受人尊敬，便是封建制度特有的本質。回頭，我們再看到現資本主義社會，有錢便受人尊敬，當然是同樣的必然現象。一個人能够對她的環境反抗什麼呢？假使她的環境要她這麼做。所以我覺得，我們也用不着去詛咒她們，因為她們原是那麼柔弱而可憐啊。

然而我也並不是没有顧及這種以愛情為麵包的青年問題，不過我覺得這個問題是不能與詛咒她們混在一起的。當然，愛情成為商品是件不好的事情，我並也覺得這不好的事情是更不好於我們一般的青年的。不過我總覺得這不是社會制裁的問題，也不是教育的問題，更不是詛咒的問題，這問題是直接關係於現社會的存在呵！想從社會制裁這點來解决這問題、决没有成效。因為在這現社會中，有誰能施其制裁？換一說，想從教育方面去消滅它，也不會有什麼成功。因為在這現社會中，教育根本已失了主宰。若是說到詛咒，那根本是不能解决什麼事情的，只不過徒然自擾一陣罷了。

假使我們要使愛情不成不商品，那………恕我在此停嘴擱筆。｜｜完｜

雅典富翁的豪舉

— 木郎

日前報載雅典電訊：

此處有大富翁大實業家名賴麻氏者，今日特發怪癖，自其住宅之樓頭，以一百五百及一千特拉格曼（希臘幣名）之鈔幣，向下散播，使路人爭相攫取。此種消息瞬忽傳佈全城，不約而集者千萬人，爭相攫取空中飛舞之鈔紙。迨警士到塲彈壓之時，爭呶已化為暴亂。遂不得不調動後備軍士，前來驅散羣衆。後警士復入賴麻之宅中，禁止其再以鈔票下擲。惟賴見警士入其室，卽將其面前堆　如山之鈔票撕裂；並向警士稱：彼對於此種齷齪錢財，深惡痛絕，並謂彼深受阿堵物之累，頗感壓倦去。警士以其神經錯亂，卽送之入某醫院。而其家族稽其賬籍，彼頃刻所散佈者，已在十萬特拉格曼以上云。

這則駭人聽聞的消息，隨着它的傳佈的力量，震撼了全世界第一地每一財迷的心竅。我們想像，當那位大富翁賴麻氏在撒着他的鈔票的時候，屋下羣衆如痴如狂地爭奪的狀態，够多麼熱烈囂亂？我不能確正那種熱狂的狀態是到了怎樣一個地步，但是我想，幾年前某烟草公司曾在上海用飛機自高空散下可換香烟的傳單，卽時在街頭引頸企望的一般男女老少的希冀的神情，或可想像現在的雅典富翁屋下的羣衆的狂態於萬一。

然而，闢開羣衆的描寫，値得我們注意的却是那位大富翁的歇斯低里地的舉動。不是心理學家，我不能確定那位富翁是否屬於變態的一種，然而至少他的神經系統突然缺乏了條理，這是毫無疑義的。往往聽見有人說，别的事情多做了，便覺得膩煩，例如飯喫得太飽了，就要打惡心，睡眠睡得太足了，也要生睡病。惟有錢財這樣東西，任憑怎樣，却没有人嫌它太多的。可是現在不然，現在也有人壓惡起錢財來了，不，非但壓惡，甚至還要把代表錢財的鈔票撕毁，這不是有違於常態的進化的嗎？　　固然，在表面上，賴麻氏將鈔票分散於羣衆，這是一種不可多得的善舉或豪舉，但細究其實，果然他是在佈賜着衆生嗎？這祇要看他對警士的談話：彼對於此種齷齪錢財，深惡痛絕……就可以知道决不是的。他並且說，「深受阿堵物之累，頗感壓倦。」是則他對於錢財的所以「深惡痛絕，」正是向來過分「嗜財若命」的反應。從佛教的理論講，這就是因果循環。我們中國古書上有一名話道「利令智昏」，也可以為賴氏的寫照。　　在中國，從來不曾聽見過像這種新聞，因此像賴氏般的「戇大」在中國也决難找到。不過，從日常生活上，我們也往往可以體味出和賴氏一樣的苦痛的心情，但我們的機遇比較小或淡漠，因此我們的感覺也就不得　淺了。

譬如某人在某日買到了一張航空獎劵，就從卽日起，到開彩日止，他幾乎是每晚上要失眠的。等到開彩後知道自已所買的號碼並没有中，他倒反而泰然了。在這幾十或幾天的焦思苦慮中，他準得减少幾磅體重。萬一他中了頭獎，這對於他的精神體力，將更是一重怎樣苛劇的麼難啊！也許我的話未免說得過火，但我還覺得是就一般的對象說的。　　然而遭受磨難的人却從不怨怪過他們所受的磨難的頒賜者。也許他們連自已的受苦是誰在作崇都不知道，當然更無從怨怪起了。　　富翁未始不可做得，財也未始不可發得，但做了富翁，有了錢財，反要受精神上的牽制或磨折，那末財富之於人，是否一種幸福，是空受了許多痛苦，連財也没有發成，而空受了許多痛苦，如買發財票者！　　於此，雅典富翁的找到了發洩痛苦的對象｜｜把鈔票撕裂，倒是聰明而又値得效法的藥方，因為至少他可以從此心無掛碍了。

處世一訣

— 雪菲

往常講究處世的，總不過是以下兩事：一是拍馬，二是吹牛。這是衆人皆知的事實。最近我才又新發展了一個處世方訣。這便無論什麼人，先要把他當作壞人看，心裏有什麼話　　於無論什麼人，切不可就隨便的　　　　對於人家的話，也不可以隨便就相信。就是說，對於無論什麼人，總要帶三分虛僞。

本來，虛僞也可歸入吹牛中的一部分，然而這裏凑有特别提出來研究的必要。何以故？因為這是普通人還不大注意的一個處世方訣。而我尤其是因為不懂這個處世方訣而受到很大的實害的人，所以對於這門秘訣特别有心得，為自。已有資格來講一講這個問題。

我的所以不懂這門秘訣而受實害的事實，就是因為我過於相信了朋友講了許多老實話，結果為這朋友所賣。由於這一經騐，我才知道說話是不能過於老實的，老實就會做上海人所謂的「曲死」。本來這是有點經騐的人都知道的，我的所以被朋友所賣，並不是什麼意外奇遇，是社會上常見之事，然而我竟不知。不獨我不知，恐怕社會上一般青年像我這樣糊塗的還多着罷。　這是個人私事，不足稱道，那末我們來講社會上比較範圍大一點的事體我們看，社會上那一件事才是眞實的。我們知道，報上廣吿根本上就没有可信的理由，他的說話，起碼要打×折。然而所謂新聞也者，又是以有「聞必錄」為原則，其所聞究屬如何，只有天知地知之了。　　那末整個社會根本都是不眞實的了嗎？是又不然。從另一方面看來，社會上事又件件是眞實的。這話怎講？這要橫的方面從利害關係組合上去看，縱的方面要從利害關係的前後的遞嬗演變上去看。我們知道，社會的組合，根本是利害關係的組合；而社會的演進，又是這利害關係的遞嬗與變化。認清了這一點，然後我們才可以把握到事實的中心。假使你能把他們中間的利害關係弄清楚，那没有一件不是很簡單的，這就是一切來赤裸裸的只有利害關係。什麼道德　　總不過是　人的，澈底的說，所謂道德情誼，根本也是其築於利害關係之上，没有利害關係，就没有所謂道德情誼。在古代是如此，要現代更是如此。假使你要丢了利害關係去從别的方面推求，那你對於一切事都會茫無頭緒，只覺左又不是，右又不是。　　世間一切事，旣然唯有利害關係才是最眞的眞實，那末我們的處世方訣便可知道了。這就是只有從利害關係中才能求到你眞正的挈友。他和你要好時，他决不是眞心愛你，而是有所利用於你；到不需要你時，他是不妨就一腳踢開你的。你假使當作他眞心待你好，因為你誠心誠意去對待他，那便大錯而特錯了，結果你一定為他所愚弄。這是一個處世要訣。

自我職業介紹

丹君，江蘇人，師範畢業，擅長國學，書法蒼秀，曾任中小學國文教員及政軍各界文牘書記公司秘書等職，如有公館學校公司及機關等須用此項人材者薪金不計，請投函本埠愛多亞路紗布交易所曹校君收轉可也。　　沈女士，江陰人，年十九歲，高小程度，現欲找一位置，職員或練習生均可，接洽處愛多亞路紗布交易所曹校君轉。　　韻清君，年三十二，中學程度，能製造各種化妝香品及藥品如本外埠實業家需聘此項人才，可函知本報業餘周刋轉。　　龍君，浙江籍，年二十九，警官學校肄業，歷任外埠警務機總稽查及保衛隊隊長等職，滬上各界欲僱稽查衛士者，請投函本報業餘周刋轉。　　棟君，年三十一，浙江人，中學程度，曾充某師部高級軍官，現欲擔任各大公館主人保衛之職，或其他相當事務，通訊處本報業餘周刋轉。　　鵬女士，粵籍，曾卒業高級中學，歷任教職員等職，今願任粵籍小學教授或家庭兒童教授，薪金如全日則三十元以內，半日二十元，通訊處本報業餘周刋轉。

小說

孤獨的人（三）

— 黛妮

（二）滬杭道上

隨卽克佳帮着效蓀料理行裝。所謂行裝也者，也簡單得很，幾套隨身衣服，日常用品，及書籍等。一切整束之後，克佳說：　　「我還是前天到杭州來的，看你兩次，老媽子說已兩天没有回來。住到家里去恐怕老祖母說我結婚的時候還東跑西跑，所以住在湖濱旅館，旣然我們明天動身，我去算清了房金，今晚上同床而眠，如何？　　「好！没有教訓完的話嗎？」　　效蓀說着笑了起來。回到寫字椅里，架起了腿，習慣地從烟罐中抽出兩枝烟來，一枝授給克佳說：　　「還是抽香烟罷。

野牛牽動了一下嘴角，把要說的話嚥住在喉頭。兩個燃上火，他就出門去了。

效蓀掠着天然鬆曲的頭髮，白色的烟噴出來，隨了春風向窗外飛散種種地　　果然，這天晚上，他們談了一夜的天，他們談到效蓀和勤菠的戀愛，「失戀是不是苦痛的」，談到克佳和靜宜的「把戲」是不是點綴人生的，一切悲哀掉在歡樂的後面。天色已不知不覺的第二天開始了。效蓀呼喚老媽子起身，梳洗完畢，趕開往上海的早車。　　效蓀雖說是養病，這般早起，到西子湖畔來後還是第一朝。　　遙望太陽從山凹中吐出來，那黄金色的光茫照到湖面上，三月的春風吹過，水面波動着柳絲的倒影，好似萬條金蛇從清澈的水底湧泳上來。效蓀抬起天然鬆曲的頭髮，輕輕地舒一口氣，在黄包車上自語着：　　「我今天認識西子的美麗了。」

車夫腿打着屁股，在晨風中很快的抵火車站。效蓀神經質地對整個杭桓暼了一眼，似乎離别新婚的妻子一樣，雖然在厭棄生活的平凡，但是三個月的勾留，情不自禁地的愛戀起來。　　「矛盾的人生呵！」克佳瞧透了效蓀的心緒，唱贊美詩似的笑着。　　在嘈雜的人羣中坐上了火車，一聲汽笛車子蠕蠕地開動。兩個人没有說話。兩種不同的思潮佔據着各人的心頭。身子隨着舒適的坐墊感到和諧的節凑，在這種安閑的環境中，將他們送入了矇矓睡鄕。　　兩旁的田嚋，屋宇，向後倒去，一列長車怒吼着前進，在嘉興車站停住的時候，他們被女子的喊聲驚醒過來。效蓀舉起頭來見對座一個女子笑容可掬的注視着，以為這女子笑他們好睡，不好意思的假裝向月台上閒眺。克佳抬了抬眼皮，仍低下頭去那女子見没有注意到自已，就靠近這隔開兩座的小桌，側着頭說：　　「克佳，到上海了。」

1934.02.01

False Capital Construction Plan

(Beiping) Since the Japanese created the puppet organization of Changchun and designated it as "Xinjing," construction has been steadily progressing. The total project cost is estimated to reach a massive 1,419,000 yuan, including 435 government buildings with a construction cost of 6,890,000 yuan and a material cost of 1,680,000 yuan. There are 500 ordinary residential buildings with a construction cost of 5,620,000 yuan. A total of 800,000 civil and construction workers, 2,348,000 construction workers, and 375,000 kiln workers, totaling 3,603,000 people, will be employed. The average daily workforce is 15,820 people, with a total wage bill of 4,196,000 yuan, including 816,000 yuan for civil and construction workers. The materials used include 22,650 cubic meters of sand, valued at 400,000 yuan, 10,000 bricks, valued at 1,500,000 yuan, 550,000 bags of cement, valued at 1,000,000 yuan, 20,000 kilograms of lime, valued at 300,000 yuan, 4,600 carloads of timber, valued at 4,100,000 yuan, and 124 cubic meters of sand and soil, valued at 300,000 yuan, totaling 7,530,000 yuan. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Chen Jitang's Plans

Cai Tingkai of the 19th Route Army Sends Telegram to Guangdong Regarding Aftermath

(Hong Kong) Cai Tingkai is still at the military camp in Longyan. On the 31st, a telegram was sent to Guangdong. Chen Jitang then summoned Weng Guiqing to headquarters to discuss the aftermath of the 19th Route Army. The Guangdong province will continue to provide food and allowances for the army's dependents. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Chen Mingshu to Visit Russia for Observation

(Hong Kong) It is heard that Chen Mingshu has left Fujian and will visit Russia for observation. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Bandit Disturbance at Yangxiwei Repelled

(Hangzhou) The He Battalion of the 4th Zhejiang Security Regiment, stationed in the western countryside of Pucheng, heard the previous night that several hundred bandits had attacked Yangxiwei, 20 li from the western countryside. The battalion immediately led troops to suppress them and engaged in a fierce battle at Xizhou for two hours, routing the bandits. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Tan Qixiu's Troops Transported to Hangzhou for Training

(Hangzhou) Of the three regiments of Tan Qixiu's troops captured in Yanping, excluding those who escaped, there are still two to three thousand men. Chiang ordered their gradual transportation to Zhejiang, tasking the Security Department with reorganizing and training them. Currently, one regiment of approximately seven to eight hundred men has been transported to Hangzhou. The Security Department has established a prisoner management office specifically for training purposes. Over a thousand more men are expected to arrive within days. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Razheng Hutuktu to Act as Regent for the Dalai Lama

President Wang Sends Telegram of Notification

(Nanjing) Guan Juezhongni, the director of the Tibetan Office in Nanjing, and others previously received a telegram from the Tibetan Silon Kasha Yicang and the entire assembly of monks, officials, and civilians, stating that Razheng Hutuktu had been elected to act as regent for the Dalai Lama and requesting central government approval. This was approved at the 145th meeting of the Executive Yuan on the 30th. President Wang sent a special telegram to Guan Juezhongni and others on the 31st to inform them. The original telegram is recorded below: To Director Guan Juezhongni and all representatives of the Tibetan Office in Nanjing, and to be translated and transmitted to the Tibetan Silon Kasha Yicang and the entire assembly of monks, officials, and civilians, the Executive Yuan's decision of the 30th, immediately approved by the National Government, to have Razheng Hutuktu act as regent for the Dalai Lama, is deeply believed that Razheng Hutuktu will be able to increase wisdom, widely implement teachings, and support the central government, in order to fulfill the utmost intention of assisting the teachings and protecting the people. This telegram is for notification. Signed, Wang Zhaoming, President of the Executive Yuan. (31st, Central News Agency Dispatch) After the death of the Dalai Lama in Tibet, New Delhi, the Lama leader of Liding Temple (two days' journey from North Lhasa) is now the new ruler, and is a living Buddha who will soon be inaugurated as regent to await the discovery of the reincarnation of the Dalai Lama. Since the passing away of the Dalai Lama, Tibetan affairs have been temporarily governed by the Prime Minister and cabinet members, while the whole country is praying for the early appearance of the reincarnated Dalai Lama. Infants born at the time of the Dalai Lama's death are being carefully examined for noticeable marks on their bodies. Several infants will then be selected and cared for for two or three years before undergoing final tests to determine the true reincarnation. (30th, Reuters Dispatch)

Yin Rugeng Inspects Zunhua

(Beiping) Yin Rugeng arrived in Zunhua from Yutian on the morning of the 31st to conduct inspections. Yin was urged by the Japanese to proceed with the handover of Gubeikou. He plans to stay in Zunhua briefly before heading to Ma Yuku to meet with Toyosawa, the commander of the Japanese garrison. Then he will pass through Ji County and Sanhe, and is expected to return to Beiping within this week. (31st, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) The issue of reorganizing the Yutian police force is currently being referred to the authorities by Yin Rugeng for instructions. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Kailuan Labor Strike Resolved

(Mine Owners Accept Union Conditions)

Majia Gou Mine Resumed Work Yesterday Morning

All Mines Will Resume Work Today

Central Government Recalls Party Affairs Personnel from Mining Area

(Tianjin) The labor strike at the four Kailuan mines was resolved on the night of the 30th after direct negotiations between Xing Sen'aide, the director-general of the Mining Bureau, and representatives of the labor union. The union representatives agreed to address the punishment of the police who fired shots, compensation for the workers who were injured or killed, and the reinstatement of the union as separate issues to be directly negotiated with the provincial government. They presented the following demands to the mine owners: (1) reinstate the unemployed workers; (2) abolish the small subcontracting system and allow the union to designate suitable individuals to take over the small subcontracts; (3) issue the two months' bonus for the 22nd year; (4) pay the workers' wages for the duration of the strike. The mine owners indicated that they could accept these conditions, provided that the workers immediately resume work, after which a contract would be signed. The worker representatives telegraphed to the various mines on the night of the 30th, instructing the workers to resume work first. On the morning of the 31st, the Majiagou Mine fully resumed work. Three-tenths of the workers at Tanggezhuang Linxi resumed work, and the rest are expected to fully resume work within one day. (31st, Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) The Central Party Headquarters telegraphed the Hebei Provincial Party Headquarters, ordering the recall of party affairs personnel from the Kailuan mining area and the temporary suspension of union activities to avoid provoking international issues and to facilitate the resolution of the labor strike. After receiving the telegram, the Hebei Party Headquarters telegraphed the mining area's party affairs instructor, Xu Wentian, to return to Beiping. The Kailuan labor strike, which lasted 17 days from the 14th to the 31st, resulted in a total loss of approximately 200,000 yuan for the mine owners, with a reduction of 300,000 tons in coal sales. Therefore, the mine owners reluctantly accepted the terms of the settlement in order to quickly end the labor strike. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Beiping Military Council Regular Meeting

(Beiping) The regular meeting of the Military Council was held this morning. Over twenty people attended, including He Yingqin, Wan Fulin, Jiang Bocheng, Ji Yiqiao, etc. He Yingqin chaired the meeting, reporting on the Sun-Ma conflict and the central government's handling of Sun's situation. They also discussed several routine cases, such as Xie Gangzhe of the Third Naval Fleet's request for supplementary soldiers' food expenses from the previous year. The meeting adjourned. (31st, Special Dispatch)

British Embassy Official Discusses Britain's Lack of Ambition in Tibet

Openedo Gan Expected to Arrive in Shanghai This Month

(Beiping) A British Embassy official stated: (1) The new British Ambassador to China, Openedo Gan, is expected to arrive in Shanghai on February 26th, proceed to Beijing in early March to present his credentials, and arrive in Beiping in mid-March to assume his new post. (2) Britain has no political ambitions in Tibet. They have not received reports regarding the independence of Southern Xinjiang and are therefore unable to comment on the true situation. The return of the Panchen Lama to Tibet, if appointed by the Chinese government, would be welcomed. (3) The revision of the Sino-British Commercial Treaty will be determined after receiving instructions from the British government. (4) The Singapore Naval Conference was a routine meeting and not worthy of attention. The content is related to international affairs and cannot be disclosed. (31st, Central News Agency Dispatch)

Japanese Hastening Repair of Jehol Motor Roads

(Beiping) The Japanese are actively developing transportation in Jehol. Most of the main and branch lines of the motor roads have been completed. The Jin-Chao railway line is being extended to Chengde and has already reached Yebaishou. It is expected to be officially open to traffic in April this year. The motor road between Chengde and Gubeikou, also being built by the Japanese army, is also scheduled for completion at the same time. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Zhejiang Province Advances Million in Military Expenses

Chiang Promises to Reimburse in Full

(Hangzhou) After the Fujian Incident, Zhejiang Province raised and advanced one million yuan in military expenses for the central government. After Lu Dipeng and Zhou Junyan met with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and explained the financial difficulties, he agreed to reimburse the full amount. The budget for this year is short by 1.3 million yuan, and a request has been made to the central government for monthly subsidies, but there has been no concrete result. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Zhang Xueliang Arrives in Hangzhou

(Hangzhou) Zhang Xueliang, accompanied by Tang Guozhen, Tan Enbo, Duan Na, and aides-de-camp Cao Fukun, arrived in Hangzhou at 4:00 PM today in two cars via the Shanghai-Hangzhou highway. Lu Dipeng, along with the Commissioner of Civil Affairs Lu Bichou and the Commissioner of Finance Zhou Junyan, welcomed him at Qingtai Gate Station. After arriving at the station, Zhang briefly interacted with the greeters before heading to the Xiling Hotel to rest. Due to the fatigue of the journey, he did not receive guests. At 8:00 PM, he went out to visit friends and enjoy the night scenery on the lake. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Shang Zhen Arrives in Beiping from Nanjing

(Beiping) Shang Zhen arrived in Beiping tonight after attending the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee in Nanjing. (31st, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Shang Zhen, upon returning to Beiping tonight, stated that the spirit of the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee was excellent, and there was considerable discussion regarding the situation in North China. Zhang's future is expected to be announced at the Central Political Council in two days. The central government is quite concerned about the Sun-Ma conflict. Chiang indicated that if Sun complies with the orders of the Military Council, the matter would be easily resolved. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Chairman Chiang Visited Lin and Wang Before Leaving Nanjing to Bid Farewell

To Head to Jiangxi After Military Deployments in Fujian

(Nanjing) Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, accompanied by his wife Soong Mei-ling, Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi and his wife, and over thirty guards, departed at 5:25 PM on the 31st aboard a specially prepared first-class train and a mixed first and second-class carriage, attached to the Shanghai-Beiping through train, to Shanghai and then Hangzhou. As few people were aware, only He Yaozu, Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua, Vice Minister of Communications Zhang Daofan, Military Vice Minister Cao Haosen, Capital Police Chief Chen Zhuo, National Government Secretary Gao Lingbai, and Lishi Society Director-General Huang Renlin saw him off at the station. Before departing, Chiang visited Chairman Lin and President Wang to bid farewell and instructed Smith to fly the Ford aircraft to Hangzhou at noon for his use. It is reported that Chiang will not stay in Shanghai upon arrival but will proceed directly to Hangzhou by train. Chiang told reporters at the station that he would first go to Hangzhou and then to Fujian. Once the military aftermath has been deployed, he will go to Jiangxi to supervise the suppression of the remaining bandits. The military operations in Fujian Province are largely complete, and the reorganization of surrendered troops is underway and should be completed soon. Kong stated that he was going to Shanghai to consult with the Shanghai banking community and not to Hangzhou. He is expected to return to Nanjing around next Monday. (31st, Dispatch)

(Nanjing) Chairman Chiang paid respects to Chairman Lin at 3:30 PM on the 31st and visited President Wang at 4:00 PM for half an hour. He then returned to the military academy to meet with Zhu Peide, Huang Musong, He Yaozu, and others, giving instructions. (31st, Central News Agency Dispatch)

Tao Shangming and Ii Wo Continue Discussions on Receiving Yuguan

Old County Government in the City to Be Received First

Hirata's Troops Withdraw to Dongluocheng

Rumors That Several Hundred Japanese Troops Entered the Pass for Rotation

(Beiping) Tao Shangming arrived in Yuguan at 8:00 AM on the 30th and met with Ii Wo at the South Sea Japanese barracks at 10:00 AM. They agreed to work with County Magistrate Yuan Tai to first receive the old county government in Yuguan City and restore the temporary public security bureau. The situation inside Yuguan City is that Hirata's Japanese troops have withdrawn to Dongluocheng. The puppet government's various agencies are still in the city and functioning as usual. Last night, a train carrying Japanese soldiers arrived at Yuguan Station, loaded with military vehicles and a large amount of supplies. It is reported that they are being transported to Cheluocheng. Tao will return to Tangshan after receiving Yuguan. (31st, Special Dispatch)

(Tianjin) Several hundred Japanese soldiers arrived in Yuguan from Jinxi Goubangzi on the 27th, along with over a dozen trains carrying military supplies such as heavy artillery. They were transported over three days and are still parked at the station unloaded. A portion of the troops arrived in Qinhuangdao on the 29th, causing widespread rumors in the Yuguan area. There are rumors that the Japanese troops are being rotated. Tao Shangming, upon hearing this, telegraphed Ii Wo for clarification but received no reply. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Bandit Liu Attempts to Disrupt Daokou-Qinghua Railway

Contact with Cheng Regiment of Henan Army

(Beiping) He Zhuguo's army pursued and suppressed bandit Liu. On the morning of the 30th, they recaptured Shexian. At noon on the 30th, a portion of Liu's bandits fled to the vicinity of Kecheng, where they were ambushed by Shi Shi'an's regiment of He's army and Bai Fengxiang's cavalry division. The bandits suffered another major defeat, with countless casualties. Most of them fled from the Jin border to the vicinity of Lujia Gua and Yin Qu, making contact with the Cheng Regiment of the Henan Army under Kui Du and Xi Bianyang. (31st, Special Dispatch)

(Beiping) Over two thousand of Liu's bandits, pressured by He Zhuguo's troops from Wu'an, completely withdrew from Shexian and fled towards the Taihang Mountains. A portion of them have crossed the Zhang River, attempting to disrupt the Daokou-Qinghua Railway, echoing the local bandits. The counties of Linxian and Weihui have repeatedly telegraphed Kaifeng for help in recent days. Liu Zhi has telegraphed the Beiping Military Council to order He's army to advance and has also dispatched Peng's regiment, together with the 84th Division, to guard the Daokou-Qinghua line. (31st, Dispatch)

Jiangxi Provincial Government Plans to Tunnel Gan River

(Nanchang) The terminus of the Nanxun Railway, Niuhang Station, is separated from Nanchang City by the Gan River. The provincial government plans to build a tunnel to facilitate transportation. The Geological Survey Institute of the Department of Construction is about to begin surveying. (31st, Central News Agency Dispatch)

He Jian Telegraphed Report of Recapturing Xiaoyuan

(Hankou) He Jian telegraphed a report of recapturing Xiaoyuan, stating that Liu, Zhu, Li, and other troops advanced in three routes, fought hard, and recaptured the area. The area is located between Yue Tong, Yi, and Wanmen and is strategically important, serving as Kong's old nest. There were puppet agencies such as repair shops and military schools, all of which were destroyed. (31st, Special Dispatch)

(Nanchang) Peng's division on the western route telegraphed that the bandits in the Jiangjunshan area had been routed, and over a thousand strongholds had been seized. The bandits are now fleeing into the deep mountains of Yongxin. (31st, Central News Agency Dispatch)

Chinese Trainees to Join British Fleet for Training

British Embassy Ordered to Contact Government

(London) It is heard that the British Embassy has been instructed to contact the Chinese government regarding the continued dispatch of Chinese trainees to the British fleet for training. (31st, Reuters Dispatch)

Hubei Headquarters Issue Proclamation to Hasten Repair of Jianghan Main Embankment

(Hankou) The headquarters issued a proclamation to hasten the repair of the Jianghan main embankment, urging its completion while the winter is clear and the water is low. It strictly prohibits the military from conscripting laborers, disrupting the embankment workers, and preventing local embankment profiteers from extorting and obstructing the work. It also allocated 100,000 yuan to hasten the repair of the highways in southern and northern Hubei, ordering the provincial government to supervise the progress. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Inner Mongolia Duoyinkuer Living Buddha Representative Zhang Shaozhou Returns to Beiping

(Beiping) Zhang Shaozhou, the representative of the Duoyinkuer Hutuktu Living Buddha of Inner Mongolia, returned to Beiping yesterday after being dispatched to Beijing. According to him, the Duoyinkuer Hutuktu Living Buddha resides in the Wudangzhao Temple, with over a thousand lamas and a total population of over three thousand, located over a hundred li northeast of Baotou, accessible by car in a few hours. His trip to Beijing was to discuss the affiliation of Wudangzhao after the establishment of the Inner Mongolia Autonomous Region Government. Before the launch of autonomy in Inner Mongolia, the temple was under the jurisdiction of the Suiyuan Provincial Government. After the establishment of the Autonomous Region Government, the Living Buddha decided to join the Region Government. His visit to Beijing involved meeting with President Wang, Minister Huang, visiting Mongolian dignitaries residing in Beijing, and contacting representatives from Shanxi several times, resulting in a satisfactory outcome. At the time of the establishment of the Autonomous Region Government, Wudangzhao will become a part of the Region Government. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Xu Zushan Visits Chiang to Discuss Funding

(Nanjing) After Xu Zushan was appointed as the special commissioner for diplomatic inspection of the five provinces of Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, Anhui, and Sichuan, Xu recently came to Beijing and has been visiting various authorities for days. Due to financial difficulties, he had to seek instructions from the government. On the 31st, he visited Chairman Chiang and reported everything. Regarding the funding, Chiang has agreed to request the government to allocate it. On the 1st, he plans to visit President Wang for instructions on policy before going to Hankou to prepare for the establishment of the commissioner's office. In the future, the diplomatic situation in the five provinces will be reported to the diplomatic authorities at any time, and diplomatic steps will be taken in accordance with the central government. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Gandhi Raises Funds to Restore Earthquake Disaster Area

Current Affairs Commentary

Criticism of Stalin's Report

Success

The dictator of the Soviet Communist Party delivered a report at the Seventeenth Congress of the Soviet Communist Party. It began by analyzing the current state of the world economy, followed by the achievements of the Soviet Union since the implementation of the First Five-Year Plan. It then provided a detailed analysis of the international political situation and stated the Soviet Union's position. The final conclusion reiterated the achievements of the Five-Year Plan and contained a slightly revolutionary tone. Overall, we acknowledge the realization of the Soviet Union's First Five-Year Plan and the Soviet people's efforts to achieve their projected ideals, and recognize their spirit as an example for all countries in the world, which is especially worthy of study and attention by the world amidst the deepening economic panic. However, there are still some things we must say.

First, since the Great Revolution, the Soviet Union has regarded itself as the leader of the world revolution. However, since the implementation of the New Economic Policy, it has focused its efforts on domestic economic construction. While superficially maintaining the banner of world revolution, it has actually been engaged in the organization of Russia itself. Any compromise is acceptable as long as it benefits Russia. Therefore, it can sell the Chinese Eastern Railway to Japan in pursuit of peace, sell oil to seek stability, conclude non-aggression pacts with Central European countries, and even express goodwill towards Italy, which stands at the opposite extreme. Not long ago, France, which the Soviet Union considered to be an anti-Soviet leader, also concluded a non-aggression pact. From all of the above, it can be seen that the Soviet Union's actual international actions are contrary to its usual theory. Stalin's report this time is also inconsistent in this regard. As for the world situation it has analyzed over the years, it often deviates far from reality. It believes that capitalism will collapse immediately and exaggerates that capitalist countries will attack the Soviet Union. In fact, the claim that capitalist countries will attack the Soviet Union is long gone. Now, the Soviet Union is improving relations with them one by one. Only Japan in the East remains in opposition. In this case, where is the reliability of Stalin's report?

Second, Stalin's report expressing deep satisfaction with the Chinese Communist Party is even more inconsistent with the facts. The Third International's misjudgment of the future of the Chinese revolution is not new. Because of its mistakes, more disputes have arisen in our country, leading to the suspicion of interfering in our internal affairs. At the beginning of the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and the Soviet Union, it was already stated that they would not interfere in each other's internal affairs and would not engage in propaganda against each other. The Soviet Union treats the United Kingdom and the United States in the same way, and even Japan in the Far East. In fact, for example, the Soviet Union cannot instruct its party members to promote doctrines that are unfavorable to their country in the opponent's country or to use illegal actions. At the same time, the opposing country must not use White Russians to form organizations and propaganda against the Soviet Union. This is common knowledge. In the past, the Soviet Union could still use the excuse that the Soviet Union and the Third International are not in the same category and that the Communist Party's organization is not under the command of the Soviet Union to shirk responsibility. But in fact, the Soviet Union and the Third International are not only the same in origin, but also act in the same way. All countries in the world are also clearly aware of this, without any doubt. However, the Soviet authorities skillfully use it to avoid excessively blatant traces. However, Stalin's report this time clearly favored the Chinese Communist Party. It not only favored it, but even vigorously promoted it and cited it as an aid. This kind of argument is both contrary to the Soviet Union's usual so-called peaceful diplomacy and has the suspicion of helping China's internal chaos and interfering in China's internal affairs. It is greatly contrary to the original intention of resuming diplomatic relations and friendship. This is what we cannot but critically criticize in Stalin's report.

We dare to tell Mr. Stalin frankly that no country in the world today can erase its past history. In other words, the boundaries between countries cannot be removed in a short period of time. At a time when national consciousness is flourishing, the Soviet Union must also devote its efforts to national defense construction. Our country has been extremely invaded by various countries. The only way out for China is to promote the inherent spirit of our nation. Sun Yat-sen had a clear teaching long ago. The Three Principles of the People, as indicated in 1927, were once acknowledged and considered correct by Lenin, the creator of the Soviet Union. In recent times, things have remained the same. The suffering of secondary colonies is even greater than in the past. Stalin's promotion of the Communist Party, which engages in murder, arson, and inciting peasant riots, not only shows that his understanding of the world situation has fallen into a mechanical and one-sided observation, but also that his observation of China has never been recognized. I cannot but have words to refute it.

Yuhsueh Railway Survey Completed

(Zhengzhou) The privately-owned railway from Yuhsien to Hsuchang has completed its base measurement, and all kinds of planned maps are now largely done. The preparatory committee was opened on the 30th in Yu to discuss the next steps. (30th, Central News Agency Dispatch)

Central Political Conference

Posthumous Honors to Yang Shuzhuang

(Nanjing) The Central Political Council held its 393rd meeting on the morning of the 31st. The committee members who attended were Yu Youren, Wang Zhaoming, Lin Sen, Zhang Ji, Shao Lizi, Chu Minyi, Shao Yuanchong, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Lifu, Fang Juehui, Jing Xiangyi, Shi Qingyang, Kong Xiangxi, Mao Zuquan, Wang Zhengting, Li Zonghuang, Gan Naiguang, etc., more than 40 people. The chairman was Ju Zheng. The resolutions were: (1) Yu Youren proposed that the Control Yuan's supervisor He Jiwu requested to resign. It was proposed to approve the request, and the supervisor Guang Lu has not yet taken office. It was proposed to open the vacancy, and it was also proposed to appoint Du Chen, Ma Hongbin, and Dai Kuisheng as the Control Yuan supervisors. The proposal was passed. (2) Liu Zhi and others proposed improving military health education and other business. The proposal was handed over to the Military Committee for reference. (3) Lin Sen, Chiang Kai-shek, Wang Zhaoming, Ju Zheng, Dai Chuanxian, Ye Chuqiang, etc., proposed that the late committee member Yang Shuzhuang was honest and upright, and his family was in dire straits after his death. It was proposed to grant generous posthumous honors. The proposal was passed. (4) The finance team's report was passed, examining seven financial cases. (31st, Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Nanjing) In addition to the publicly announced resolutions of the Central Political Council on the 31st, there was also a proposal by the National Economic Council to establish a Central Land Administration. The resolution was to hand it over to the Legislative Group for review. Second, four members, Liu Zhi, Zhu Jiahua, Chen Lifu, and Zhou Qigang, proposed to control the handling of food in order to promote rural revitalization and drafted an outline of measures. They requested a public resolution. The resolution was to hand it over to the Economic Committee for review. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Ministry of Finance Revises Tariff Regulations

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance instructed the Director General of Customs that the revision of the tariff regulations should be adapted to the times, and those that are not very compatible with the current trade situation should be slightly changed. Therefore, with reference to the recent market conditions of kerosene and gasoline, the existing import tax has been levied. Kerosene is levied at 0.1137 gold units per unit, and gasoline is levied at 0.47 gold units per unit. Now, the revised and increased tariff regulations are as follows: 520 mineral gasoline and naphtha gasoline, (including various unnamed engine fuels) A. Boxed, 2.10 gold units per 100,000 gallons, B. Bulk, 2.00 gold units per 10 US gallons. 532 Kerosene (including other mineral oils for ignition, with a specific gravity of 0.78 to 0.90) A. Boxed, 1.80 gold units per 100,000 gallons, B. Bulk, 1.70 gold units per 100,000 gallons. The above new tariff regulations shall be implemented from February 1934. Please comply and instruct all customs offices to comply. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Preparing for Negotiations on Sino-British and Sino-American Treaty Revisions

(Nanjing) Both the Sino-US and Sino-British treaties have reached their expiration dates. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued a note to both countries to conclude new treaties. The US government replied that it had accepted the note. The British Embassy in China has issued a note to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating that it has telegraphed the Chinese note to the British government and will reply after receiving instructions. According to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the principles for concluding a new treaty have been roughly prepared. Although the issue of consular jurisdiction is not related to the commercial treaty itself, it is related to it. When China and the United Kingdom and the United States revised the issue of consular jurisdiction in 1930, the countries also indicated that they would gradually abolish it as China's judicial reforms progressed. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is prepared to raise the issue of abolishing consular jurisdiction when discussing the commercial treaty with the United States and the United Kingdom. As for when the Sino-US negotiations will officially begin, it is still difficult to decide. (31st, Special Dispatch)

Economic Committee Plans to Hold Plenary Session

Standing Committee Decides on Levee Protection Plan

(Nanjing) The Economic Committee's third standing committee meeting on the 27th decided on matters such as this year's national highway and water conservancy construction, as well as the selection and establishment dates of the Jiangxi Northwest offices. However, important cases that the standing committee cannot resolve, such as the allocation of US cotton and wheat loans requested by various parties and the establishment of various control committees, all await the decision of the entire committee. It is planned to convene the first plenary committee meeting in Nanjing around March 10 to discuss the aforementioned major cases. In addition to the 34 official members and 5 standing committee members, three legislators specially appointed by the Legislative Yuan will participate in the plenary committee meeting, as well as one or two representatives from each provincial government (director of the construction department or industry department) to clarify the construction situation in each province and the steps to be taken. Notification letters will be issued within days. (31st Dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Economic Committee's third standing committee meeting decided that the Yangtze River bank protection plan should focus on planting turf on the levee body as the sole important project for levee protection, and the Jianghan Engineering Bureau will be responsible for handling it. The required funding is still being estimated. (31st Dispatch) (Nanjing) The Economic Committee will conduct salt land reclamation in Lianghuai and will convene a meeting of relevant agencies in the coming days to discuss a design plan. (31st Dispatch)

Provincial System to be Reformed Soon

Legislative Yuan to Amend Provincial Organization Law

(Nanjing) The reform of the provincial system was proposed and passed again at the Fourth Plenary Session. According to a certain person in charge, the reform of the provincial governor system had already been passed by the Third Plenary Session and submitted to the Executive Yuan for its opinions. The Executive Yuan proposed that the civil affairs, finance, education, and construction departments should remain, and a director of the political affairs department should be added to assist the governor in handling provincial affairs. During the discussion at this Fourth Plenary Session, slight modifications were made. In addition to the education and construction departments remaining, a deputy governor and a political affairs department were added. The political affairs department is divided into general affairs, civil affairs, and finance divisions, with the deputy governor concurrently serving as the director of the political affairs department, assisting the governor in handling all matters in order to concentrate authority and achieve practical results. It is heard that all parties attach great importance to this plan and are strongly urging its implementation. In the shortest possible time, the Legislative Yuan will be instructed to amend the provincial organization law and re-formulate it for implementation. It is expected that this will be realized in the second half of this year. (31st Dispatch)

Jin Xi's Arrest: Ministry of Foreign Affairs Lodges Protest

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has lodged a strong protest with the French and Japanese embassies regarding the illegal arrest of Jin Xi by the Shanghai French Concession police in collaboration with the Japanese consulate. (31st Central News Agency Dispatch)

Central Government Plans to Deal with Xinjiang Incident

He Yaozu and Huang Musong Recommended for Review

(Nanjing) It is heard that the Central Political Council has formulated a plan to deal with the Xinjiang incident and the southern Xinjiang issue, which will be submitted for discussion at the meeting on the 31st. It was decided to recommend He Yaozu and Huang Musong for review. Furthermore, Chairman Chiang summoned Gong Bicheng, the representative of Xinjiang Province stationed in Nanjing, on the 31st to inquire about the situation in Xinjiang. Gong reported in detail on the news from southern Xinjiang and requested the government to allocate 2 million to the Suiyuan-Xinjiang Motor Vehicle Company to develop transportation in Xinjiang, in order to fundamentally resolve the disputes in Xinjiang. (31st Dispatch)

1936-1937

Comparison of US and Japanese Navies

Japan has the Advantage in Destroyers and Submarines

(Tokyo) Previously, on the 27th, Mr. Uchida Shinya raised a question at the Budget Committee of the House of Representatives. Therefore, the Navy made a public statement to the Budget Committee on the comparison of the naval strength of Japan and the United States after the completion of the second supplementary accounting of the Japanese Navy. The current status of battleships is as follows:

United States: 15 ships, totaling 455,400 tons

Japan: 9 ships, totaling 272,070 tons

As of 1936, the United States had 7 warships that exceeded their age limit, while Japan had 4. Due to the London Treaty, the construction of replacement warships was not permitted. Therefore, by the end of 1936, their actual strength was:

Japan: 5 ships, 154,750 tons

United States: 8 ships, 251,600 tons

The ratio is 62%. The strength of aircraft carriers as of 1936 is as follows:

Japan: 5 ships, 78,420 tons

United States: 5 ships, 119,800 tons

The ratio is 65%. The strength of Class A cruisers is as follows due to the restrictions of the London Treaty:

Japan: 12 ships, 107,800 tons

United States: 16 ships, 152,650 tons

(Two more are under construction)

The ratio is 71%. Class B cruisers are as follows:

Japan: 17 ships, 98,799 tons

United States: 14 ships, 20,500 tons

The ratio is 89%. The comparison of destroyers within the age limit is as follows:

Japan: 76 ships, 105,111 tons

United States: 46 ships, 67,360 tons

The ratio is 1.56. Japan shows an absolute advantage. Japan also shows an absolute advantage in submarines:

Japan: 35 ships, 52,553 tons

United States: 24 ships, 32,670 tons

The ratio is 1.61. The total strength of auxiliary ships (cruisers, destroyers, submarines) is as follows:

Japan: 140 ships, 364,259 tons

United States: 100 ships, 363,180 tons

Although Japan has 40 more ships, the tonnage is about equal. (31st Joint Dispatch)

Soviet Stratosphere Exploration

Three Aviators Perish

Ascended 12.87 Miles

(Moscow) The Soviet stratosphere balloon "Siriyahes" has met with misfortune. The three aviators in the balloon chamber have been found on the Moscow Katzabon Railway and have all perished. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

(Moscow) The Soviet balloon "Siriyahes," which set a new record for ascending into the stratosphere yesterday, has been searched for all night without any trace. Radio communication with the balloon has been interrupted since last night. It is generally believed that the balloon must have fallen into the forest, but airplanes and other search parties have been unable to locate it. There is currently a thick fog here. The Soviet Director of Civil Aviation has issued a radio message ordering all flight stations to assist in the search. Stalin and others are particularly anxious. (31st National Dispatch) (Moscow) The Soviet stratosphere balloon "Siriyahes" ascended at 9:07 this morning. By 11:45, it had reached a height of 67,568 feet, or 12.87 miles. At noon, the balloon began to descend and landed safely in the afternoon. During the ascent, the three people in the balloon chamber communicated with the ground continuously. Another Soviet balloon, "Soviet," had previously ascended to a height of 11.5 miles. This record has now been broken by "Siriyahes." (30th Reuters Dispatch)

Opening of the New German Parliament

Hitler Elaborates on Political Achievements

National Socialism Saves the Country from Peril. Diplomacy Based on International Harmony

(Berlin) Today marks the first anniversary of German Chancellor Hitler's rule. The German Parliament convened a special meeting with great solemnity. The parliament was filled to capacity, and the people gathered outside the parliament were also overflowing. When the Chancellor arrived at the parliament, the people cheered and paid their respects. When the Chancellor entered the parliament, everyone in the chamber stood up and raised their hands in the party salute.

Chairman's Speech

First, General Göring, the chairman of the parliament, gave a speech, stating the achievements made by the National Socialist government in the past year. He said that even in a superficial comparison, it can be found that the development of the country's various affairs in the past year has made the German nation, under the command of the National Socialist leader, seem to have been reborn. In terms of diplomacy, Germany has also been able to make countries admire Germany's attempts, beliefs, and achievements in a very short period of time. Göring also said that all members of the government today share the same political and philosophical beliefs and serve the same work program. This is the first time in German history. Therefore, the only task of the German Parliament from now on is to implement the national construction program promulgated by the leader Hitler. (30th National Dispatch)

Hitler's Speech

Then, Chancellor Hitler took the stage to give a speech, briefly stating that the history of the world in the past fifteen years has been controlled by two facts: first, the authority of the state has been undermined by Marxism; second, the Versailles Treaty adopted intimidating and fraudulent means in politics and economics, causing people to lose faith in the world order.

Abhors the Treaty of Versailles

The Treaty of Versailles caused people to lose all hope, resulting in resentment. The German people have lost faith in "justice" and harbor resentment towards the international situation. The Communist Party took the opportunity to rise and engage in its tricks.

Rescues People from Disaster

The National Socialist Party rose to protect Germany from being ravaged by the Communist Revolution. Saving Germany is therefore saving the entire world from being devastated by the world revolution.

All Ethnic Groups are Respected

National Socialism is the embodiment of "national will." The racial ideology it holds does not despise other ethnic groups. This kind of thinking is very helpful to world peace. Those who forever discriminate between victorious and defeated countries will never achieve as good results as racial ideology.

Eliminates Class Struggle

Hitler then narrated

The achievements of the National Socialist Party in its first year in power, saying that the National Socialist Party's ambition is to gain the trust of the entire nation. Precisely because the whole people trust it, it can break party disputes and eliminate Marxism. We have occupied the premises of various labor unions, but the intention is to oppose class struggle, not to oppose workers.

Consolidates Religious Belief

Speaking of religious issues, Hitler said that the various factions of the German Evangelical Church have been merged to form a national church. This is only to consolidate the belief of the Evangelical Church. However, the various churches should also respect the National Socialist state. (Havas Dispatch)

Monarchy Becomes a Relic of the Past

Hitler also said, "Recently, an ideal has emerged in the country, saying that the German nation cannot live and work in peace unless it is governed by a traditional monarch. Today, I should protest against this fallacy, because in this year, we have consolidated the authority of the state and the government, so that those who wish to see the old inferior policies return will not be able to achieve their goals. We have considerable respect for the past monarchy, but the question of what kind of political system the country should use to govern is no longer within the scope of discussion today.

Not for Economic Survival

Hitler then discussed economic issues. He said that in the past year, the government's subjective policy has been the state, not surviving for the economy, and the economy is certainly not surviving for capital. Both the economy and capital are things that serve the state. (National Dispatch)

Willing to Maintain Friendship with Russia

When speaking of diplomatic issues, Hitler said that Germany is willing to get along peacefully with all countries,

Regardless of its political system. Therefore, Germany strives to maintain friendly relations with Soviet Russia. However, Germany cannot tolerate communist propaganda in Germany. This is the same as the National Socialist Party not being tolerated in Soviet Russia. (Havas Dispatch)

Abandons Old Grudges Against Poland

Hitler also expressed his opinion on the German-Polish peace treaty. He said that even if there are unavoidable disputes between the two countries, it cannot be said that there is no way to reconcile them. Everything depends on human effort. (National Dispatch)

No Intention of Infringing on Austrian Sovereignty

Hitler said that the issue between Germany and Austria is a regret for the German government, but claimed that the blame does not lie with Germany. The rumors that Germany is infringing on Austrian sovereignty are unfounded and unverifiable. It can also be seen from this that a broad and fundamental ideology has permeated the entire German nation and cannot be limited by national borders. The people there share the same blood, the same language, and for hundreds of years, their country has been an inseparable part of our country.

France and Germany Should Join Hands

Hitler also praised the friendship between Germany and Italy and praised the achievements of Mussolini. Finally, he said that the best result of the dispute over equality of rights is the cooperation between Germany and France. For hundreds of years, the men of the two countries have shed blood on the battlefield from time to time, but ultimately there can be no fundamental change. France is afraid that its borders will not be guaranteed, but who in Germany has threatened it?

Saar Does Not Need to Vote

Moreover, after the Saar region is returned to Germany in the future, there will be no more so-called territorial issues between the two countries. Therefore, the Saar region should be returned as soon as possible, so that the atmosphere can be cleared as soon as possible and permanent peace can be established. (National Dispatch)

British Mediation is Appreciated

Hitler continued to say that Britain's willingness to mediate between Germany and France is deeply appreciated. Germany will study the recent proposals put forward by Britain in the long term. Finally, Hitler said that the reason why Germany withdrew from the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference is because Germany's security and honor cannot be satisfied to the minimum extent through this path. However, the German people are still willing to do their best to cooperate with all nations. Hitler's conclusion was well received, and applause was endless. (30th Havas Dispatch)

Passed on Third Reading

Law on Transforming Germany

Administrative Control of Various States Directly Under the Central Government

Independent Representative System Abolished

(Berlin) This afternoon, the law on transforming Germany, proposed by Interior Minister Frick at a special meeting of the Parliament, was passed on third reading by a unanimous standing vote. It stipulates that the independent representative system of all states in Germany shall be abolished, and the power to control all provinces shall be completely vested in the central government. The parliaments of all states shall be dissolved, and the remaining administrative organs shall be subordinate to the central government in Berlin. Frick, in one fell swoop, placed the chief officials of the various states appointed by Chancellor Hitler last year directly under the control of the central government. The new law will take effect immediately after being passed by the Parliament.

Britain Slightly Relieves Anxieties

It is a pity that Hitler's words and deeds do not always match

(London) Yesterday, the speech given by German Chancellor Hitler at the opening of the Parliament has slightly relieved the anxieties of British newspapers. The British newspapers praised Hitler's remarks expressing hope that France would abandon its old grudges. However, it is a pity that Hitler's remarks on Austria were not of a reassuring nature. The Morning Post alone expressed doubts about Hitler's remarks, saying that his words and deeds do not always match, and deeply hoped that Hitler's words were sincere and not just for diplomatic purposes. The Daily News regrets that Hitler did not mention Germany's return to the League of Nations. The Times said that Hitler could carry out policies of internal reform and external reconciliation with greater freedom and power than before. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

(London) There is no shortage of people who praise Hitler's speech, but some people also say that the practical results claimed by Germany are also pleasing to the ear. Germany still has 6 million unemployed people who are living in extreme poverty, and the continued observation of other countries has also aroused many suspicions in Berlin. The newly established German-Polish Non-Aggression Pact is a victory for Hitler, allowing him to prove his desire for peace. However, disarmament is still a matter of speculation, and the activities of the National Socialist Party in Austria are also a very serious problem. The Balkan countries are now watching the dispute between Germany and Austria with deep concern, because Austria's independence is closely related to their economic cooperation and political harmony. Austrian Chancellor Dr. Dolfuss gave a speech yesterday, saying that his struggle is against the wrong world view, and that he is now fighting to defend Christianity and resist heresy. Therefore, there is no doubt that foreign countries still hold a deeply distrustful view of National Socialist Germany. (30th Reuters Dispatch)

Solving the Disarmament Problem

Contents of the Italian Memorandum

Mainly Through Ordinary Diplomatic Channels

Establish a Convention Between Countries First

Rome The Italian memorandum aimed at solving the disarmament problem was released today. It states that if the situation improves slightly soon, the disarmament problem can be solved separately by all parties. However, in the current environment, it is doubtful whether Germany can reach a compromise without re-arming. Therefore, the problem is how to maintain armaments within the scope of the agreement without allowing them to expand. The Italian government believes that a convention can be established based on conditions that can satisfy the opinions of various countries. The convention must include the following four points: (1) Abolish chemical warfare; (2) Prohibit bombing of civilians; (3) Limit the armaments of countries not bound by treaties to the existing level; (4) Limit the land warfare equipment of countries not bound by treaties to the existing level. As for Germany's request to equip an army of 300,000 men, the Italian government believes that in view of the current state of armaments in various countries, even if Germany's request is allowed, Germany may not be more privileged than the plan proposed by British Prime Minister MacDonald. The Italian government also believes that the reorganization of Germany's naval status should be left to the next naval conference for discussion. The Italian government finally expressed its intention to faithfully abide by the Locarno Treaty and stated the necessity of exchanging opinions at present, so that the diplomatic authorities or prime ministers of Western governments can hold a meeting and invite representatives from other relevant countries to participate. (31st Reuters Dispatch)

British Memorandum

No New Suggestions

Acknowledges German Equality in Armaments

Resolutely Opposes Trial Period

(London) The content of the British memorandum to Germany, France, Belgium, the United States, and Japan yesterday on disarmament has been announced by newspapers. No new suggestions have been seen. The memorandum firmly rejects the idea of a trial period, declaring that Britain, in principle, acknowledges Germany's equality in armaments and suggests that the so-called transitional era should begin immediately. During this era, a compromise plan should be agreed upon for Germany's rearmament and other countries' reduction of armaments. It also suggests that countries should quickly organize international management of armaments affairs. According to the Daily Herald, Britain advocates the demobilization of Germany's stormtroopers and similar organizations. Although the newspaper did not criticize it, it hopes that the British memorandum can help the progress of negotiations. (30th National Dispatch)

Germany Returns British Military Drum

Booty from the European War

(Berlin) This afternoon, a ceremony was held at the Ministry of the Army to return the military drum of the British Army Gordon Regiment, which was captured near Ostend in 1914, to British Sir Hamilton. The ceremony was very solemn. First, Army Chief Baron von Blomberg gave a speech, expressing admiration for the bravery of the soldiers of both armies. Then, British representative Sir Hamilton gave a reply, briefly stating that he was deeply grateful for President Hindenburg's agreement to return the previously captured military drum. He thanked on behalf of the British military and was particularly grateful for the hospitality of the German Army Chief and the military department. After the ceremony, he immediately proceeded to the Presidential Palace to pay his respects to President Hindenburg. (31st National Dispatch)

Hawaii for Hawaiians

Roosevelt's New Appointment

(Washington) President Roosevelt decided today to appoint Hawaiian Poeing Dexter as Governor of Hawaii, succeeding Guder. (30th Reuters Dispatch)

US Shipbuilding Bill Passes House

Building 102 New Ships in Five Years

Adding 1,184 Naval Aircraft

Maintaining Hegemony in the Pacific

(Washington) Today, the House passed Vincent's US Large Navy Plan, a proposal to build 102 new ships, and an amendment to purchase 1,184 naval aircraft. The bill is unlikely to face opposition in the Senate. When Vincent spoke in the House, he said that the US Navy's strength was inferior to that of the Japanese Navy, so the US influence in the Far East was gradually disappearing, and the US was now very isolated in the international community. He also said that the US should pay special attention to the naval conference in 1935, because if it does not make efforts to rectify at this time, the US will lose all naval authority. Britain and Japan are making every effort to expand their naval strength in accordance with the treaty-specified quotas. In the current situation, it is difficult to mobilize the US in the event of an incident. In his speech, Vincent also strongly advocated that the president should have full authority to build new ships and repair all old warships. Congressman Britten was a strong supporter of Vincent's proposal. According to Vincent's proposal, the US must rush to build 65 destroyers, 30 submarines, 6 cruisers, and 1 aircraft carrier. As for the amendment, it is planned to allocate 90 million to add 1,184 naval aircraft. (30th National Dispatch)

Naval Conference Next Year

Concerns About Discussion of the Far East Issue

Foreign Minister Hirota Aims to Restore National Credit

Arikawa Believes Not Holding a Conference is the Best Option

(Tokyo) The House of Peers reconvened at 1:40 PM. Former Foreign Minister Kozawa Akira took the podium and stated, "I am not here to ask accusatory questions, nor to question past achievements, but to inquire about the government's aspirations. I have heard the speeches of the Prime Minister and the Foreign Minister. It can be said that future policy relies entirely on diplomatic efforts to sweep away thorns and open up difficult situations. However, the future is vast, and difficulties are unavoidable.

Next year is the scheduled date for the naval disarmament conference. If both Japan and the United States follow the intentions of their respective navies and attend the conference, it is conceivable that the conference will inevitably break down. In this situation, optimists say that even if the conference fails, there is no fear of war, nor any competition in shipbuilding. Pessimists, on the other hand, worry about everything. So what should be done? If holding the conference leads to a breakdown, it would be better not to hold it at all. It is more necessary to engage in prior negotiations. Only after negotiations should a decision be made on whether to hold the conference. It would be safer not to hold the conference, as this is not only the case for Japan, but for any opponent, there is no hope of a good outcome from such a conference. Therefore, it is better not to hold it.

Secondly, it is also possible that the Far East issue may be raised at next year's disarmament conference. It was discussed at the Washington Conference, so there is a precedent for this. Regarding this point, the government's aspirations should be decided in advance, as Japan bears the full responsibility for maintaining peace in the Orient. It is not necessary to only discuss the Far East issue. As for the naval issue, Japan should prioritize its own position. If the 5:5:3 ratio is not conducive to maintaining peace in the Far East, then a ratio sufficient to maintain it must be demanded, which goes without saying. Next, regarding the issue between Japan and the Soviet Union, I believe that there are no major issues between Japan and the Soviet Union that cannot be resolved without resorting to war. Japan and the Soviet Union are neighboring countries and have not yet severed diplomatic relations. Furthermore, Foreign Minister Hirota has already stated that he will strive to maintain peace through diplomatic efforts, which I strongly support. If Japan believes that it is impossible to coexist with the Soviet Union's communist system, that is a misguided view. If the Soviet Union is willing to wage war in order to complete the communization of the Orient, that would be extremely reckless.

Regarding the trade issue, I believe that today's situation is by no means a crisis, and a crisis may not even come to pass. Even if it does, diplomatic efforts should be used to overcome the difficult situation. If a third country violates our will, provokes us arbitrarily, and causes war, then decisive measures may be taken. Even at the very end, we must not resort to anything other than peaceful means. This has already been stated by the Prime Minister and the Foreign Minister, which I admire.

Regarding the rise and fall of the world's trust in Japan, I feel that it is related to Manchuria. If Manchuria is established and stable, then Japan's position can be said to shine brightly in the world. Completing the construction of Manchuria will lead to a satisfactory relationship between China and Japan. Fortunately, Manchuria is steadily progressing towards completion. I deeply appreciate the efforts of the government and the military, and hope for even more complete results."

Mr. Kozawa's speech took some time, and he slowly stepped down from the podium. The responses from the Prime Minister and the Foreign Minister are as follows. First, Foreign Minister Hirota replied, "It is inconvenient to respond one by one. My feeling is like walking on thin ice. I believe that a war will not occur over the Far East issue, and I now believe that there is no need to worry. At this time, it is necessary to enhance the nation's credit." Prime Minister Saito also gave a simple reply, thanking Mr. Kozawa for his encouragement. The meeting adjourned at 3:05 PM. (United Press, 31st)

(Tokyo) At today's House of Peers meeting regarding the South Seas Mandate issue, Foreign Minister Hirota, in response to a question from former Foreign Minister Kozawa, replied that he does not adhere to the League of Nations' sovereignty theory, the mandatory power's sovereignty theory, or the Allied Powers' joint sovereignty theory, but insists on basing it on the facts of the Great War, stating that it is Japan's right of possession. This is particularly noteworthy, as when the Allied Powers reached an understanding on the disposition of the former German territories, they decided to place the South Seas Islands under Japan's jurisdiction. Afterwards, at the Paris Peace Conference, the form of mandate was adopted. Therefore, Japan is not necessarily satisfied with the mandate policy, but it does not change the fact of possession. Having understood and accepted this explanation, even though Japan has withdrawn from the League of Nations, Japan does not lose its right of possession. (Dentsu, 31st)

Hirota Studies Pro-American and Pro-Russian Policies

Re-Proposing Arbitration Treaty to the U.S.

Planning to Establish a Demilitarized Zone with Russia

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota, in his response to Ryuuji Nagashima of the Seiyukai at the general budget meeting on the 30th, stated that the government is currently working hard to study effective methods for peaceful relations with the United States and for limiting border defenses between Russia and Manchuria. It is reported that the Foreign Minister is considering the following policies towards the U.S. and Russia:

Policy Towards the U.S.

The Foreign Minister intends to have Ambassador Saito, after his appointment as ambassador to the United States, meet with President Roosevelt to explain Japan's peaceful diplomatic policy. If he can obtain President Roosevelt's understanding, he will not hesitate to conclude a Japan-U.S. arbitration treaty in order to implement active peaceful relations.

Policy Towards Russia

The Foreign Minister believes that the adjustment of Japan-Russia relations lies in first resolving the outstanding issues between the two countries. Therefore, when the Russian side proposed concluding a non-aggression treaty in the previous year, Japan politely refused. However, the opportunity to renegotiate the China Eastern Railway is near, and the Soviet Union's attitude towards Japan shows signs of softening. The causes of conflict between Japan and Russia within "Manchuria" can also be expected to disappear. In order to maintain peace in the Far East, Japan demands that the Red Army withdraw from the Russian-Manchurian border, expand the spirit of the Treaty of Portsmouth, clearly define the national border between Japan, Manchuria, and Russia, and establish a demilitarized zone within 150 miles of the border to avoid conflict. In order to realize this policy, Japan will propose the establishment of a border commission after the outstanding issues are resolved. (United Press, 31st)

Roosevelt Formally Approves

Currency Bill Becomes Law

All Cash in the Country Becomes State Property

President Has the Right to Control the Price of Silver

(Washington) President Roosevelt's currency bill, having been passed by both the Senate and the House of Representatives, was signed by the President this month. According to this law, all cash and gold coins within the country become state property. The U.S. dollar cannot be exchanged for cash, and the President also has the right to regulate the gold value of the U.S. dollar. The President will now issue multiple orders to regulate the implementation of the currency law, such as setting the value of the U.S. dollar at 60% of the gold value, and establishing an exchange equalization fund of $200 million, which are especially important. (Havas, 30th)

Promulgation of the Gold Ordinance

(Washington) The gold ordinance issued by President Roosevelt today allows the Federal Reserve Bank to exchange gold for government gold certificates, in such quantities as the Treasury Department deems necessary to clear international debts and maintain equal purchasing power of various U.S. currencies. The bank may buy gold overseas and within the United States for the above purposes. Gold may be retained or transported or imported or withdrawn or stored in external or internal accounts. Imported gold, if sealed in customs, may be re-exported without a permit; otherwise, a permit is required. (Reuters, 30th)

Sterling Cooperation Possible

(London) Today, Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain stated that there is a possibility of cooperation between the British Exchange Equalisation Fund and the U.S. Stabilisation Fund, as Britain is not using this fund to make special changes to the pound. Chamberlain's statement can attract the attention of both Britain and the United States, or secretly conduct negotiations, and can reassure the general public and reduce the degree of future conflict. (National News Agency, 30th)

Domestic and International Impact

(Washington) The Currency Act signed by President Roosevelt this afternoon is the most important law in the United States for several generations. This law confirms the reforms that the American financial and economic system has undergone since March 1933, and will have a very significant impact on the internal economic development of the United States and on international monetary and economic relations. The new law defines the new dollar as a non-redeemable currency, and gives the U.S. state ownership of half of the world's cash, that is, all public and private gold reserves in the U.S. The President, according to this law, may freely change the gold content nominally belonging to the currency, that is, the Treasury also becomes a true bank issuing banknotes, and the government may also use a $200 million exchange equalization fund to directly intervene in the financial markets of various countries around the world. Also, since President Roosevelt stopped the gold standard last year, people's hearts have been unsettled, resulting in major confusion in international monetary and commercial relations. Since the promulgation of the new law, this phenomenon has been stopped. However, the dollar price set by the new law is clearly below the price naturally determined by supply and demand in the exchange market, which may inevitably cause a disturbing factor. The U.S. Treasury's intervention in the international gold and exchange markets is sufficient to exacerbate the unequal distribution of cash in the world. From an economic point of view, after the devaluation of the dollar, American export businesses will be excited, and the large number of unemployed people in the United States are eager to find work. For a very long time, they will not demand higher wages according to the new dollar price, which is especially convenient for the U.S. export industry. However, because the United States devalues its currency to develop export trade, it will also reduce import trade because of the devaluation of the currency, because the value of foreign goods is thereby increased. This matter harms foreign countries and is likely to cause international disputes, but in the United States, debtor countries will find this

Page 10

easier to repay interest. The above is in terms of foreign influence. Domestically, private debt, originally calculated in gold dollars, is now repaid in devalued dollars, and all debt is naturally reduced. The beneficiaries and victims are divided into two categories. Farmers trapped by taxes and industrial companies trapped by bond interest are all blessed by the new law. Conversely, the victims are mortgage creditors and those holding public debt. In short, the middle class engaged in savings and laborers who depend on wages for a living are harmed because wages cannot rise with the cost of living. In addition, the new monetary system contains the potential for monetary expansion, especially the potential for lending expansion. The country's economic activity will thereby be strongly stimulated. In addition, the new law can only have the effects described above, both domestically and internationally. (Havas, 30th)

Roosevelt's Birthday

More Than 200,000 Congratulatory Telegrams

(Washington) Today is President Roosevelt's 52nd birthday. Approximately 200,000 congratulatory letters and telegrams have arrived from all sectors of the world, and hundreds of kinds of birthday gifts, mostly cakes. One cake weighs 250 pounds, and another bread weighs 255 pounds. A congratulatory letter from Alabama was signed by 40,000 people and was 1,180 feet long. About 6,000 banquets were held throughout the United States, raising millions of dollars for the treatment of polio patients at Warm Springs, Georgia. (Reuters, 30th)
