Taking over the various passes of the Great Wall

Stuck in a State of Stagnation

Unreasonable Demands Made by the Japanese Side

Bandits and Soldiers肆意 Disturbing the Locality

The Yutian Mutiny Has Yet to be Resolved

Beiping Correspondence: Since the recovery of the war zone, due to the agreement, it has been impossible to restore order. Ordinary bandits and frustrated elements are taking advantage of this situation to cause disturbances. The various passes of the Great Wall, the gateway to the war zone, although the Japanese side has promised to hand them over, repeated negotiations have been fruitless due to diplomatic changes, and the takeover is indefinite. The Yu Guan takeover negotiations have been deliberately hampered by the Japanese side. Yi Wo, the chief of the Japanese Special Service Agency stationed in Shanhaiguan, has made various unreasonable demands that are difficult for us to accept. The situation has now completely stalled. Progress has been made on the issue of taking over the Gubeikou Pass since Yin Rugeng, the administrative commissioner of Ji-Mi, went to Gubeikou to negotiate with the Japanese military authorities. However, there are still many problems that make it difficult to implement immediately. Furthermore, the Japanese military has built military installations at various important passes. At the same time, the puppet state has set up checkpoints and administrative agencies at various passes. Even if the passes are taken back, they will be nominally controlled. The conflicts between the two sides may arise at any time. A grave mistake has been made, and future troubles are inevitable. The bandits in the war zone have been suppressed in the past, and most of them have been eliminated. However, the remaining bandits are still entrenched in the Jie Lingkou area and can come south to cause trouble at any time. The bandit troops of Li Jichun and Shi Yousan, who were formerly incorporated, have been reorganized into security teams. They have neither gotten rid of their bandit nature nor given up their political motives. They arbitrarily expand their forces and disturb the locality. The authorities can do nothing about it. The recent unrest in Yutian, which has turned into an unprecedented catastrophe, was caused by the security teams that were reorganized from this type of bandit troop. It is found that Shi Yousan previously recruited bandits in Qinhuangdao, intending to cause trouble. After the war zone was taken over, this group of bandits was reorganized into a branch of the security team after repeated negotiations, led by Zhang Futang, and stationed in Yutian. Since this bandit troop was incorporated, on the one hand, it has continued to communicate with Shi Yousan, waiting for an opportunity to act, and on the other hand, it has recruited troops and extorted money arbitrarily to expand its strength. The gentry and wealthy people in Yutian have suffered greatly. In the middle of this month, this bandit troop suddenly recruited 300 bandits from the Tangshan area and opened them up to Yahong Bridge, east of Yutian County, for large-scale extortion. Merchants and residents could not bear the disturbance and fled. The bandits became angry and attacked the town in its entirety on the night of the 19th, looting and burning it. The entire town was looted, and most of the houses were burned to the ground for two days and nights. The Yutian County militia, seeing the town being robbed, united and confronted the bandits. The situation is serious. The authorities are restricted to the war zone and cannot take decisive action against the bandits for the time being. Yin Rugeng, the administrative commissioner of Ji-Mi, has been asked to consult with the headquarters of the 51st Army and the commissioner of the Hebei Provincial Government to find a way to negotiate and avoid further suffering. As a result of the mediation of all parties, the bandits have all retreated to Yutian City. Yahong Bridge is temporarily patrolled by 30 guards from the Commissioner's Office, who are working with the militia to maintain order. All follow-up arrangements will be discussed at length. In recent days, the situation in Yutian and Yahong Bridge has eased. However, the bandits are demanding to be reorganized into a regiment. The authorities are still considering this matter, and the location of the bandit troop's relocation has also become a problem, which may be difficult to resolve properly for a while. In short, the war zone is full of thorns, the problems are complex, and the hidden dangers have not yet been eliminated. (Reached January 28)

Sun Dianying's Troops Attack Ningxia Provincial Capital

Main Force Along the Helan Mountains

Besieging the Provincial Capital, Fierce Fighting

Beiping Correspondence: The conflict between Sun Dianying's troops invading the west and Ma Hongkui's troops has lasted for more than ten days. They have successively occupied various towns in Ningbian and penetrated deep into the interior. Although various parties have stopped them, they have not stopped their advance. Sun's attitude is outwardly gentle but inwardly firm. He has repeatedly shown his obedience to the central government and the Beiping authorities. He has repeatedly telegraphed that he has ordered the front-line troops to stop heading west and requested that the Ning army be ordered not to attack again. He has also sent representatives Hu San and Wang Shiping to urge Song Zheyuan and Han Fuqu to mediate for him. In fact, the military operations have not stopped at all. Moreover, his use of troops is unpredictable and purely guerrilla warfare, which makes the Ning army exhausted in dealing with it. Since occupying Dengkou, his cavalry army, Yu Shiming's troops and Yang Hou Shaozi's bandit troops, etc., have gone south along the Yellow River, crossed the river in separate routes, besieged Pingluo, and raided Li Gangbao and Hongshanbao. The main force then secretly marched west from Dengkou, heading south secretly along the Helan Mountains. The area is sparsely populated and transportation is inconvenient. Sun's army went south along the foot of the mountains, marching at night and resting during the day. People and ghosts did not know about it until they approached the Ningxia provincial capital and launched an attack. The Ning army was strained because Pingluo and Li Gangbao were in dire straits, and they tried their best to fight the enemy there. After several days of fierce fighting, they barely held off Sun's army around the 20th, and their formation was slightly boosted. However, on the 26th, Sun's army, Liu Yueting, which had secretly marched from the Helan Mountains, suddenly arrived near the Ningxia provincial capital, occupied the Beita area outside the city, and besieged the provincial capital. At dawn on the 27th, they carried cloud ladders and secretly climbed the city. They were discovered by the Ning army, who fired machine guns from the city and sent troops to intercept their retreat. The fighting was extremely fierce, and both sides suffered heavy casualties. Currently, Sun's troops are still entrenched in Fengdengbao, Beita and other places northwest of Ningyuan, and they are attacking the city from time to time. The situation in Ningyuan is still tense.

The central government has formulated a plan for the conflict between Sun and Ma. On the one hand, it has removed Sun's concurrent post as the director of the Qingxi Reclamation Office to eliminate the idea of Sun's troops heading west and to eliminate the cause of the dispute. On the other hand, it is trying to transfer Sun's troops elsewhere to seek a fundamental solution. The Pingfang authorities, in accordance with the instructions of the central government, are trying to stop the conflict between the two sides and have sent representatives to Taiyuan Guihua to consult with Yan in Jin and Fu in Sui on a solution. However, Yan claimed to be ill, and the representative in Bing has not yet obtained any essential information. He is staying in Bing to await orders. The representative in Sui, Men Bingyue, has gone to Bao and is in contact. There is no news of his return to Ping in the shortest possible time. Wang Shiping, Sun Dianying's representative in Ping, visited He Yingqin yesterday and asked He to send personnel to Dengkou. Wang telegraphed to Sun, inviting him to Dengkou to consult on the issue of ceasing fire and withdrawing troops. He has agreed to Wang's request to send personnel, but as of today, the candidates have not yet been selected. Whether this matter can be realized is still unknown. (Reached January 30)

Jiangxi Eastern Suppression of Red Army Forces Advance Towards Western Fujian

Going Along the Jiangxi-Fujian Border to Longyan

Jointly Attacking the Red Bandit Base Area

Nanchang Correspondence: At the beginning of the Fujian Mutiny, the Northern Route Army in eastern Jiangxi, in addition to Jiang Dingwen, Wei Lihuang, Zhao Guantao, and other troops advancing south from northern Fujian towards Fuzhou, Wu Qiwu, Zhou Hunyuan, Mao Bingwen and other columns remained in towns and villages at the junction of Jiangxi and Fujian to prevent harassment by bandits and to disrupt the rear. Since Jiang, Wei and other troops recovered Zhangzhou and Quanzhou, the remnants of the 19th Route Army retreated to Longyan, attempting to hold out in a corner. In order to completely resolve the rebellion, the central government ordered the various columns on the Jiangxi-Fujian border to advance south from eastern Jiangxi towards the Fujian border, and to encircle Longyan with the central troops from Zhangzhou and Quanzhou. However, Jianning, Taining, Ninghua, Qingliu, Liancheng, Tingzhou and other places on the border between western Fujian and southeastern Jiangxi are all bandit areas, that is, the bases where the puppet 1357 Army Corps recuperated and waited for an opportunity to move during the Fujian Mutiny. The Northern Route Army must carry out a thorough suppression before entering Longyan. Therefore, Commander-in-Chief Chiang, in order to achieve both goals, ordered the Wu, Zhou, and Mao columns to depart from Lichuan to western Fujian in early January. The Huang, Fu, and Huo Divisions advanced to Zhangcun and Hengcun, where Taining and Jianning border Lichuan, on the 21st and engaged in fierce battles with Zhu Mao's various forces. Because of the repeated disastrous defeats in eastern Jiangxi last year, coupled with the exhaustion of supplies, the bandits' spirit was completely lost and they were no longer as stubborn as before. The central army, since the Xun Kou, Xiao Shi, and Xu Du campaigns, had reversed the atmosphere and eliminated the fear of bandits. Therefore, although the bandits had been recuperating for a month, they were still not enough to match the central army's strength. Each division advanced south step by step. After crossing Guangze, Taining, and Jianning, they could then reach Tingzhou and Liancheng to reach Longyan. According to a victory report sent by the forward enemy of the Northern Route Army yesterday, "Fan Songfu, Zhou Hunyuan and other troops engaged in fierce fighting with the puppet 135 Army Corps in Xikou, south of Guangze, on the 27th. As a result, a large number of bandits were killed and thousands of guns were seized. The bandits' strength is indeed diminishing day by day." (January 29)

Inner Mongolia's Request for Autonomy (Continued)

Mongols Still Disagree with Central Government's Regulations

The above three stages represent the process by which Minister Huang and the Bailingmiao Autonomy Conference Presidium discussed and agreed on the Mongolian autonomy measures. Now, the most important points of these measures will be explained separately below:

A. Regarding organizational regulations, the aim is to divide the leagues and banners of Xilingol and Chahar into the Mongolian First Autonomous Region, and the leagues of Ulaanchab and Ih Juu, as well as the Tumed, Alxa, and Ejine banners, into the Mongolian Second Autonomous Region. Each region will establish a regional government, directly under the Executive Yuan, to manage the administrative affairs of each league and banner within its respective region. In cases involving provincial affairs, they will consult with the provincial government. A joint office will be established between the autonomous regions to handle common matters. The jurisdiction and governance rights of each league and banner will remain as before. What is added for the Mongols is simply a regional government above the leagues and banners. Its authority is limited to managing the leagues and banners within its region, and each league and banner should still govern its original Mongol population. In cases involving provincial affairs, they must consult with the provincial government. On the one hand, it continues the old system and respects natural conditions, without hindering the provinces and counties. On the other hand, the regional government can supervise the leagues and banners to reorganize administrative affairs and unite to resist foreign aggression.

B. Regarding the regulations for establishing counties, it stipulates that "no more counties or administrative bureaus shall be established within the borders of the Mongolian leagues and banners." Counties are organizations specifically for managing inland immigrants, as detailed previously. Where inland immigrants are densely populated, county administrations have been established. All uncultivated areas, in fact, cannot be cultivated further. The inland merchants and people in uncultivated areas are currently managed by nearby counties, so there is no need to add more county administrations, which would only cause pain to the Mongol banners.

C. Regarding the regulations for land, it stipulates that "all existing wasteland in Mongolia shall be designated as Mongolian pasture areas and never be cultivated. The already cultivated land will be properly reorganized. Before the reorganization, the inherent rights of the Mongol banners over the land, minerals, mountains, forests, rivers, and lakes within their borders will remain as before, and the existing levies will continue to be collected. The existing private rents of Mongolian officials and people will be guaranteed." Most of the existing uncultivated land in Mongolia is desert and cold land, unsuitable for cultivation, and the area is extremely limited. The Mongol people are also our compatriots, and in the period when they cannot be quickly converted to farming, pasturelands should be reserved for them to maintain their livelihoods. Even considering our vast country, there should be adequate pasturelands as a source of camels, horses, cattle, sheep, hides, wool, meat, and dairy products. Therefore, all existing wasteland should be designated as Mongolian pasture areas to develop the local economy through improving animal husbandry and establishing related industries. As for the already cultivated land, the management methods vary from place to place, and disputes between Mongol and Han people frequently arise, which is not good for the local area. Therefore, appropriate measures should be taken to reorganize it. Before the reorganization, all existing rights and interests of the Mongol banners and Mongolian officials and people over the land should be protected.

D. Regarding the regulations for taxes, it stipulates that "all taxes within the pasture areas shall be collected by the autonomous region government according to unified methods detailed by the government. All tax collection bureaus and checkpoints established by the provinces and counties within the pasture areas shall be abolished. The Mongol people shall only bear burdens to the Mongol banners, and the provinces and counties shall not impose additional burdens. The land, mineral, mountain, forest, and river taxes collected by the provinces and counties within the Mongol banner territory, as well as other taxes, shall be jointly collected by personnel dispatched by the autonomous region government, and the proceeds shall be divided equally." Currently, the burdens on the people in uncultivated areas vary greatly. After the establishment of the regional government, methods should be found to standardize them. The tax collection bureaus and checkpoints established by the provinces and counties in uncultivated areas are few in number. To avoid double burdens on the people, they should be abolished. The Mongol people are managed by the Mongol banners and already bear considerable burdens, so the provinces and counties should not impose further burdens, which would overburden the people. In recent years, the central government has stated that education, industry, transportation, and other undertakings in Mongolia are all funded by the central government, but in reality, it is only empty promises. Moreover, it is inappropriate for the local area to completely rely on central government subsidies. The Mongol banners have a precedent for dividing local tax revenues. Therefore, it is proposed to divide half of the local tax revenues collected by the provinces and counties within the Mongol banner territory to build local undertakings with local tax revenues, so that Mongol and Han residents can benefit together. Otherwise, the Mongol banners and Mongol people will always be backward, which is not good for the local area.

The above fourteen items are the most important points of the autonomy measures agreed upon in Bailingmiao, all based on past practices and current factual needs. The Bailingmiao Autonomy Conference initially advocated for unified organization, Mongol-Han cooperation, and a high degree of autonomy, which could not be established. This method of regional and provincial coexistence, division of labor, and cooperation can still be a good strategy to resolve various Mongol border disputes and enable Mongol and Han residents to coexist and prosper.

(3) Key Points and Impact of the Central Political Council's Decision on Autonomy: The eleven articles of the Mongolian autonomy measures decided by the Central Political Council on January 17 contain many points that do not conform to the Mongolian situation. The important points are excerpted from the original text as follows:

1. The scope of the Mongolian Autonomous Region shall be limited to areas without established county administrations.

2. Two districts shall be established in each of Chahar Province and Suiyuan Province.

3. Areas in Chahar and Suiyuan provinces where county administrations have already been established shall belong entirely to the provincial administrative region.

4. The Alxa and Ejine banners, originally under Ningxia Province, shall not be included in the scope of the autonomous region (the above is Article 3 of the measures).

5. The Mongolian Autonomous Region shall adopt a two-level system of districts and banners (Article 4 of the measures).

6. With the approval of the Central Government, the local provincial government may be authorized to handle matters with special characteristics within the Mongolian Autonomous Region.

7. Various Mongolian banner administrations within the Mongolian Autonomous Region shall still be managed by the provincial government under the authorization of the Central Government.

8. All Mongolian banner administrations in areas where county administrations have been established shall be handled by the local provincial government.

9. The Central Government may entrust the provincial government to represent the Central Government and guide the Mongolian regional government in handling local autonomy (the above is Article 7 of the measures).

10. All taxes shall be divided into national taxes and local taxes. Local taxes shall be collected by the provincial government in areas where county administrations have been established and by the autonomous region government in areas where county administrations have not been established (Article 8 of the measures).

11. Mongolian banner areas without cultivation and without county administrations shall primarily engage in animal husbandry, supplemented by farming. People of the Republic of China, regardless of ethnicity, who have resided continuously in this area for more than one year shall have the right to engage in nomadic grazing and cultivation (Article 9 of the measures).

If the above provisions are implemented, the impact will inevitably lead to the following results:

A. The leagues and banners will be eliminated. The situation of the leagues, banners, provinces, and counties has been detailed previously. According to the above-mentioned Articles 1 and 3, "the scope of the autonomous region is limited to areas without established counties, and areas where counties have been established belong entirely to the provincial administrative region." In a broad sense, all areas where the power of the county reaches belong to this category. Therefore, within the two provinces of Chahar and Suiyuan, there are arguably no areas without established counties. Where will the autonomous region be established? In a narrow sense, the so-called areas where counties have been established should refer to areas that have been cultivated. In that case, 80 to 90 percent of the Tumed Banner in Chahar, and 50 to 60 percent of the Ulaanchab and Ih Juu leagues have been cultivated. The uncultivated areas are only the scattered places in the Xilingol League, the northern part of the Ulaanchab League, and the Ih Juu League and the Tumed Banner of Chahar. Establishing an autonomous region in these areas means that its area is not as complete as the original area of the leagues and banners. Furthermore, according to the above-mentioned Articles 2 and 5, "two districts shall be established in each of Chahar and Suiyuan provinces" and "the autonomous region shall adopt a two-level system of districts and banners," which means that one league or one banner is an autonomous region, and the leagues and banners have no room for existence. If it is said that they still exist, then the Mongolian side will have a dual organization, which will only increase disputes. According to the above-mentioned Articles 6, 7, and 9, various Mongolian banner administrations within the autonomous region must be subject to the control of the provincial government. Judging from the past situation of provinces and counties encroaching on the Mongol banners, it is inevitable that they will be completely replaced in the future. Such an autonomous region is far inferior to the original leagues and banners. What is the Mongol people's purpose in seeking it? Moreover, the above-mentioned Articles 4 and 8 stipulate that "the two special banners of Alxa and Ejine shall not be included in the scope of autonomy" and "Mongolian banner administrations in areas where counties have been established shall be handled by the local provincial government." Isn't this dividing the Mongolian banners that originally belonged to the leagues or were directly under the Central Government and incorporating them into various provinces? Even Mongolian banners forming a separate system cannot avoid exploitation by provinces and counties. Once they are under the jurisdiction of the provinces, there is no reason for their complete existence. In short, once the autonomy measures decided by the Central Political Council are implemented, the original status, area, and authority of the leagues and banners will be greatly reduced. In the future, they will only disappear and have no hope of prosperity.

B. Pasturelands are shrinking daily. The situation of Mongolian land has been briefly described earlier. Furthermore, in the past, Mongolian pasturelands were vast, so there was no aversion to cultivation. Some even invited inland farmers to cultivate, which proves that the Mongols have never excluded inland immigrants. However, in recent years, cultivated land has become increasingly vast, and pasture areas have shrunk. The Mongol people are also lacking in livelihood skills, leading to difficult livelihoods. This is why they have called for stopping land reclamation and preserving pasturelands. This is a request to the Central Government and the people of the country to reserve a lifeline, with no intention of resisting inland reclamation farmers. This pitiable situation should be understood by all benevolent people. If the above-mentioned Article 11 is followed, "Mongolian banner areas without cultivation shall primarily engage in animal husbandry, supplemented by farming. People of the Republic of China, regardless of ethnicity, who have resided continuously in this area for more than one year shall have the right to engage in nomadic grazing and cultivation," then inland people will inevitably migrate to Mongolian land in large numbers. After residing for one year, they can freely engage in nomadic grazing and cultivation. There are already a considerable number of inland merchants and people residing in Mongolian pasturelands. After the implementation of this measure, if millions more migrate, there will be no place for the Mongol people to produce enough food. The Mongol people cannot change their occupations to farming and industry for the time being, which is impossible in reality. At that time, they will either become bandits or fall into destitution. Regardless of the impact on the border situation, it seems inappropriate in terms of human feelings. This measure, although seemingly beautiful in form by not distinguishing between ethnicities, actually endangers the lives of the Mongol people.

C. Tax revenues are completely lost. The income from uncultivated areas in Mongolia has always been managed by the Mongol banners themselves. The Mongol banners also have various collections and divisions in cultivated areas, as detailed previously. According to the above-mentioned Article 10, "Local taxes shall be collected by the provincial government in areas where county administrations have been established and by the autonomous region government in areas where county administrations have not been established." Then what the regional government collects is only the income that the Mongol banners currently manage themselves. All the income from the Mongol banners in areas where counties have been established will be completely transferred to the provincial government. How will the Mongol banners, which rely on this income to maintain themselves, survive? If it is said that the provincial government can return it to the Mongol banners after collecting it, then based on the past facts of provinces and counties deducting the land rent and land prices that the Mongol banners should have received, it is unbelievable. After this provision is implemented, the Mongol banners will completely lose their tax revenues. Isn't this the opposite of what the Mongol people are seeking?

The above are the inevitable consequences of the implementation of the autonomy measures decided by the Central Political Council, which cannot be resolved by empty words. The Mongol people are seeking improvement but will suffer losses. Even the most foolish people would not dare to accept it.

(4) Request for Remedy: The eleven articles of the Mongolian autonomy measures agreed upon in Bailingmiao have not been approved by the Central Government, and the eleven articles of the Mongolian autonomy measures decided by the Central Political Council contain many points that do not conform to the Mongolian situation. This Mongolian autonomy issue, which concerns the country and the local area, cannot be shelved and ignored. In addition to sending letters and telegrams to the heads of various leagues and banners to request instructions, the representatives can only earnestly request your esteemed office to find a way to remedy it quickly. If you take into account the difficulties of the Mongols and still approve and implement the eleven articles of the autonomy measures agreed upon in Bailingmiao, then the Mongols will sincerely comply and will not fail to live up to the Central Government's good intentions in implementing support. Otherwise, please pay attention to the following three points, formulate appropriate measures, and implement them quickly, which will also benefit the border situation and be fortunate for Mongolia:

1. Please guarantee the original status, area, rights, and interests of the leagues and banners.

2. Please grant each league and banner a unified organization to implement autonomy and jointly resist foreign aggression.

3. Please ensure that each league and banner is forever free from the encroachment and oppression of provinces and counties.

(5) Important Statement: Many people in the country have misunderstandings about the Mongolian request for autonomy and the rejection of the autonomy measures decided by the Central Political Council. Therefore, several points are solemnly stated as follows:

1. The Mongolian request for autonomy is to gather the strength of various leagues and banners to jointly resist foreign aggression and is by no means a separatist movement.

2. The Mongolian request for autonomy seeks the coexistence and prosperity of border ethnic groups and has no intention of excluding inland immigrants.

3. The Mongolian request for autonomy seeks the common security and progress of all Mongols and is not for the benefit of a few individuals.

4. The Mongolian request for autonomy seeks a fair solution to the dual organization of leagues, banners, provinces, and counties and does not oppose the current authorities of provinces and counties.

5. Minister Huang did indeed promise to establish two autonomous region governments and joint offices in Bailingmiao. He also approved to do his best to comply with the cases of stopping land reclamation, pasturelands, and dividing local tax revenues. This can be proved by the thank-you telegrams sent by the heads of various leagues and banners after Minister Huang reviewed and approved them.

6. The autonomy measures decided by the Central Political Council do have the risk of eliminating the original leagues and banners, opening up existing pasturelands, and depriving the Mongol banners of their tax revenues. Therefore, they dare not accept them and are not misunderstanding anything, let alone making trouble unreasonably.

I have carefully examined that the Republic of China has been established for twenty-three years. Mongolia has supported the Central Government consistently, but the Central Government only relies on the provinces, believing that the Mongol people are untrustworthy. Therefore, all plans and propaganda to support Mongolia are equivalent to drawing cakes. Now that Mongolia has been forced to request autonomy, the results are worse than before. Looking to the future, I want to cry but have no tears. Therefore, I dare to lay bare my heart and clearly state my case, respectfully requesting your understanding of my foolish sincerity and a quick remedy. Then the day when Mongolia does not perish will be the year of gratitude. Respectfully submitted to Chairman Lin of the National Government, Representatives Zhao Taibao, Linqin, Suludai, and Jiyatu of the Ulaanchab League in Beijing, Representatives Senggelinqin, Bulintoktokhu, Nasenderleyuer, Baiyincang, and Ayulezhana of the Ih Juu League in Beijing, Representatives Mao Ertesuoer, Gongchongkeluo, and Hasaoqier of the Chahar League in Beijing, Representatives Bayar and Changsen of the Tumed Special Banner in Beijing, Representative Su Baofeng of the Ejine Special Banner in Beijing, Director Wu Heling of the Joint Office of Mongolian Leagues and Banners in Beijing, Deputy Directors Chen Gengyang and Qichangshan, Representatives Dai Qinglian, Wu Yunpeng, He Yongxin, Guan Baojia, Bu Wenlin, and Enhe Amur. (End)

Armed Clash with Bandits on Songhui Road, Songjiang

Near Songhui Villa on Songwei Road, last night, Niu Jinggao, deputy squad leader of the Special Service Team of the Songjiang County Public Security Bureau, led four team members on patrol when they suddenly saw shadows in the dark, indicating that people were ambushing there with strange movements. Deputy Squad Leader Niu shouted at them to stop for inspection, but four people dashed out and fled westward. Deputy Squad Leader Niu bravely pursued them. Two people in the rear turned around and opened fire. Niu immediately ordered a counterattack and reported the situation to the Songhui Villa telephone exchange, notifying the military and police agencies to intercept them. For a time, bullets flew everywhere, causing a disturbance all night. The bandits' trail disappeared. It was later learned that two of the resisting bandits had jumped onto the roof of an elderly woman surnamed Liu that day and hid there after jumping down, only leaving at dawn.

Fellow Townsmen in Beijing Request Permission for Rickshaw Pullers to Own and Operate Their Own Vehicles

The Songjiang County Government, based on the "Measures for Cracking Down on Rickshaws Soliciting Passengers" proposed by the Sanyou and Hezhong Rickshaw Companies, ordered the bureau to crack down on unauthorized rickshaws. Some argue that most of the unauthorized rickshaw pullers in Songjiang have accumulated capital to own their own vehicles and hire people to register and operate them under the name of "rickshaws." Although this may be slightly non-compliant in terms of administrative management, the rickshaw pullers also have the hardship of avoiding heavy rentals and seeking self-reliance. If the measures proposed by the rickshaw companies are hastily implemented, it will not only affect the livelihoods of the unauthorized rickshaw pullers, but also suppress the self-reliance of laborers and block the tendency for rickshaw pullers to own their own vehicles, which is inconsistent with the principles of the Kuomintang. Therefore, the original situation should be considered and methods should be devised to manage and support them. At the county party and government meeting on January 17, it was proposed that "in addition to the two rickshaw companies, a certain number of rickshaws in the city should be allowed to be owned and operated by rickshaw pullers with licenses." At that time, the county government only decided that "the county government will investigate the case and submit it to the province for instructions." It is now learned that fellow townsmen Pu, Gao, Xu, and Lu in Beijing are also very sympathetic to the proposal at this party and government meeting. Therefore, they have jointly submitted a petition to the provincial authorities, ordering the county to determine the number of rickshaws and allow rickshaw pullers to own and operate their own vehicles with licenses.

Suzhou's Population Has More Men Than Women

The Wu County recently completed its population census. Yesterday (31st), the Public Security Bureau reported to the county government that there are a total of 72,703 households in the urban area of Suzhou, with a total population of 192,136 men and 144,341 women, a difference of 47,795 more men than women.

Thieves Involved in Robbery Cases in Shanghai Escorted Back to Face Justice

The thieves involved in the robbery cases at No. 301 on Shanhai Pass Road, No. 247 on Fujian Road, and the Xifu clothing store next to the Yong'an Company near the Xinza Road intersection in Shanghai were arrested by the Huangdai Public Security 9th Sub-bureau in Jinshan Village. Xu A'gen was already escorted back to Shanghai by the Xinza Concession Police last month. Later, the Huangdai 9th Sub-bureau received a notice from the Xinza Concession Police that Xu's accomplices were also coming to Huangdai. The sub-bureau immediately dispatched police to pay attention. The day before yesterday (30th), two people came from Wangting to Xu A'gen's home in Huangdai and were arrested. They confessed that one was Zhou A'mao and the other was Sun Shaobing, and that they had come to Xu's house to retrieve a handgun. They were handed over to the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday (31st), the Shanghai Special District 1 Court sent a document and dispatched personnel to Suzhou to escort Zhou and Sun back to face justice.

Fire Burns to Death

The house of Xie Shuisheng, a villager of Gao Jingcai in the Shanren Bridge District, was burned down the night before last due to carelessness in using fire for warmth. Xie and his wife, Liu, were severely burned. Their six-year-old son, Ruijin, did not manage to escape and was burned to death. When the body was exhumed, the face was unrecognizable, and the hands and feet were burned off, like a piece of charred wood. Yesterday (31st), the procurator of the local court went to inspect the scene and then the body was collected.

Extortion and Fraud in Wuxi Result in Imprisonment

Chen Leigong and Su Wencai, who were from out of town, extorted 20 silver dollars from Shi Hu, the wife of the owner of the Wan Chengyu South-North Goods Store outside the South Gate, under the pretext of reporting a smuggling case. Shi Hu twisted Chen into the Public Security 1st Sub-bureau, reported it to the General Bureau, and transferred him to the County Court for trial and detention. Su Wencai was also arrested and detained by the court and prosecuted together. Judge Lai has repeatedly held court hearings, and the debate has concluded in the case. It is now learned that yesterday was the date for sentencing in this case. Judge Lai ordered Chen and Su to be brought to court. Chen Leigong and Su Zhicai were each sentenced to two years and eight months of imprisonment for extortion and fraud. After the sentence, they were ordered to be returned to custody to await the expiration of the appeal period before being sent to prison.

Surveying of the Circular Lake Road Begins

The construction of the Circular Lake Road in this county is a cooperative effort between the government and local people. The county government is responsible for the road construction project, while the bridge and embankment projects are funded by local fundraising. County Magistrate Yan Shenyu believes that the construction of this road will not only enhance the scenic beauty of the lake and mountains, but also revitalize the city. Therefore, he especially went to the province to meet Chairman Chen last month and personally reported the construction plan. Chairman Chen greatly praised it. After County Magistrate Yan returned to Wuxi, he immediately ordered the Technical Office to draft a budget, deciding that the cost of the road earthwork and foundation project was 7,000 yuan, and the cost of acquiring privately owned land was 5,000 yuan, which was included in the budget and submitted to the department for approval. He also used 250 yuan of surveying funds and sent engineers from the Technical Office, such as Jin Xinjing, to hire boats and bring surveyors, setting off yesterday (31st) to survey from Binjie Mountain, passing through Yuantouzhu, Zhongdu Mountain, Wanqingtang, and then to Guanshe Mountain, Qitang, Chongshan, and other places. The estimated survey period is more than two weeks. In the future, it is planned to build a long embankment from the foot of Binjie Mountain to the opposite bank, with bridges in the middle, and to build a long bridge from Yuantouzhu to Zhongdu Mountain and from Zhongdu Mountain to Wanqingtang. However, it is estimated that each bridge will require at least 50,000 yuan in construction costs. It is also heard that County Magistrate Yan believes that the Xian-Chun and Tong-Yang roads are the only way to reach the urban area from the Circular Lake Road, but these two roads are too narrow. Therefore, he has specially ordered the third and fourth district chiefs to be responsible for widening each of these two roads by two meters to facilitate traffic.

Major Fire at the City God Archway in Hangzhou Yesterday Morning

At 1:50 AM yesterday (31st), a fire broke out at the Chunji Sock Factory at No. 17 City God Archway Street in Hangzhou due to carelessness in using the stove to dry shoes. Due to the cold weather, the reporting of the incident by the on-duty police was slightly delayed, leading to a conflagration. The fire was unstoppable. The fire brigade rushed to the scene with various foreign-style fire engines to put out the fire. It took about three hours to extinguish it. Those affected were awakened from their sleep, and the cries of the old and young were extremely miserable. Moreover, many of the items snatched out were stolen by thieves. According to a subsequent investigation, a total of 15 shops and houses were burned down, with losses of more than 20,000 yuan.

To the Editor,

This is completely untrue. There is no establishment of land bureaus in these seven counties. This must be a rumor. I am sending this letter to correct the record. I hope you will publish it.

Sincerely,

The Secretariat of the Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau

China National Aviation Corporation's Newly Purchased Aircraft Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday

The China National Aviation Corporation's No. 16 Sikorsky aircraft, used for the Shanghai-Guangdong air route, encountered an accident near Dongqishan, close to Zhapu, leaving only the No. 17 aircraft to fly back and forth on the Shanghai-Guangdong route. Therefore, they purchased a new twin-engine aircraft from the Sikorsky factory in the United States, which was loaded onto the "Peter Maersk" cargo ship of the Andersen Meyer trading company and transported to Shanghai. The cargo will be picked up today (the 1st), transported to Longhua Airport, assembled, and test-flown.

Economic Cooperation Movement

(Begins Today)

Purpose: To explain the meaning of economic cooperation

Mission: To arouse the attention of society

In recent years, rural areas have gone bankrupt, industry is sluggish, and people's livelihoods are becoming increasingly difficult. Crisis looms, and the situation is unimaginable. The China Economic Credit Cooperative, recognizing this, is implementing economic cooperation as a means of self-help and mutual assistance. This allows members to save a small amount of money each month, providing appropriate relief and security from business operations and consumption to entertainment, from unemployment and illness to old age, and from children's education to family finances after death. Therefore, it directly protects the lives of individuals and indirectly promotes the welfare of society, which may well be a good way to solve national economic problems. However, the term "economic cooperation" is not well understood by society. Therefore, the cooperative proposed to launch an economic cooperation movement for two months starting from February 1st of this year, to explain the main purpose of economic cooperation on the one hand, and to gather opinions and benefits on the other. It has gained the sympathy of all sectors. Participating organizations include the Ministry of Industry, the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Municipal Social Bureau, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, etc. On the central government side, there are Chairman Lin, President Wang, Secretary-General Chu, Minister Kong, Minister Chen, Minister Zhu, etc. In Shanghai, there are Mayor Wu, Secretary-General Yu, Director Wu, Director Pan, Director Wen, Director Cai, etc. Leaders in Shanghai, such as Zhang Gongquan, Lin Kanghou, Du Yuesheng, and Wang Xiaolai, all support and participate, in order to arouse the attention of society.

This economic cooperation movement focuses on written publicity and theoretical elaboration. During the period of the movement, special supplements will be published in major newspapers, in which experts and celebrities will be invited to write articles, and contributions from all walks of life will be welcome. The cooperative's economic cooperation is based on cooperative methods to improve the inherent defects of the existing economic system and achieve the goal of mutual assistance. This is because the current economic system, with capitalism as its focus, takes free competition as the principle in all aspects of production, distribution, transaction, and consumption, which leads to unequal wealth, unequal distribution, unequal transactions, unequal production, and unequal consumption. In short, it is inequality of survival. This not only makes the poor feel pain but also adversely affects the rich. Economic cooperation aims to break this contradiction, so that wealth can be used properly to promote the comfort of our lives and bring society into a realm of mutual assistance.

New System of Weights and Measures to be Implemented Starting Today

Announcements issued by the Social Bureau and Jianghai Customs

The Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau, in order to promote the new system and abolish the old system, has issued a notice to all merchants and residents of the city, requiring them to comply with the regulations and implement the new system starting from the first day of this month. The Deputy Commissioner of Customs of the General Affairs Department of the Jianghai Customs also issued a notice yesterday stating that, starting from today, import and export goods will be calculated using the new system of weights and measures, and the equivalent number in the old system of weights and measures must also be indicated. The two announcements are copied below.

Announcement by the Social Bureau

The Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau issued Announcement No. 615 yesterday, stating: "The purpose of weights and measures is to provide accurate information about items. Standardizing instruments and processes will ensure uniformity across the region, facilitating daily use. Since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, it has actively engaged in construction, promulgating laws and regulations and promoting the new system. This bureau was ordered to handle this matter and, with the approval of the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce, designated July 1st of the 20th year [of the Republic] as the deadline for completing the standardization of weights and measures in this city. Numerous earnest announcements have been issued, and the Municipal Weights and Measures Inspection Office has dispatched personnel to conduct inspections. Now that the deadline has long passed, while many businesses have adopted the new system of weights and measures, there are still many who have delayed making changes, using the failure of customs, tax, and salt administrations to implement the new system in advance as an excuse. The Ministry of Finance issued Instruction No. 8683 in July of last year, instructing its subordinate agencies to comply with the new system by February 1st of the 23rd year at the latest. It then re-emphasized this instruction to all subordinate agencies with Secret Order No. 1697 on December 27th. Now that customs, tax, and salt administrations have complied with the new instruments within the specified time limit, there is no longer any question. All businesses still using the old instruments should immediately comply and switch to the new system to uphold the laws. Anyone who dares to deliberately violate this will be dealt with according to the law without leniency once discovered. In addition to ordering the Municipal Weights and Measures Inspection Office to intensify its efforts, this announcement is hereby issued, ordering all merchants and residents of the city to comply without fail. Take heed."

Announcement by the Jianghai Customs

The General Affairs Department of the Jianghai Customs issued a notice regarding the implementation of the new system of weights and measures, requiring temporary indication of the equivalent number in the old system of weights and measures. The notice stated: "The new system of weights and measures is scheduled to be implemented on February 1st of this year. This customs has already issued Announcement No. 1328. Starting from the date of implementation of the new system of weights and measures, for three weeks, for goods transported from domestic ports, the waybill must clearly indicate the new system of weights and measures and the equivalent number in the old system of weights and measures separately. All merchants are required to comply. This announcement is hereby issued. Zhou Ji, Deputy Commissioner of Customs, General Affairs Department."

Wang Xiaolai Urges Sun Dianying by Telegram

Obey the Central Government and Withdraw from Ningxia

The Western Border is Now Devastated

It is Inadvisable to Disrupt the Overall Situation with Military Force

Since the conflict between Sun Dianying and the Ma forces in Ningxia, the situation has gradually become serious. It is learned that Sun Dianying telegraphed Wang Xiaolai and others yesterday, stating that he had been ordered to move to Suiyuan but was attacked by the Ma army, requesting instructions on whether to advance or retreat. Wang replied with a telegram of advice yesterday. The exchange of telegrams is recorded below.

Sun Dianying's Telegram

(Omitted above) After resisting Japan in Rehe, we withdrew to the border of Chahar. Then, due to the Chahar Incident, we were ordered to move to Suiyuan and cultivate the land in Qingxi. After the order was issued, we prepared to travel west, hoping to find a way to serve the country and have the opportunity to serve. However, because of my lack of virtue, I was not understood by the Ningxia and Qinghai authorities, which led to their severe rejection. The mission of my army is only to cultivate the land, and to use cultivation to strengthen border defense. I have no ambition to seize territory, and I have never seized territory in the past. However, the Ningxia and Qinghai authorities immediately used this as an excuse to oppose us, raising the banner of resistance and rejecting us outside the border. The central government seeks compromise, but the parties involved do not realize their mistake. As a result, for several days, I have stopped the army from advancing, wandering in Baotou and Suiyuan, with tens of thousands of soldiers gathered in the desolate area. In addition, our clothes are thin and supplies are scarce. During this severe winter, soldiers' fingers and feet are frozen, and we hear about it every day. Sitting in the sand, they often speak bitterly. Seeing this, I am heartbroken and have no words to comfort them. They rely on each other in hunger and cold, with both love and pain. At this time, if we want to follow the order and travel west, we will face the enemy's attack. It is impossible to live in the wilderness. It is difficult to advance or retreat. Before, I consulted with Mr. Yan Xishan and asked to open up a fertile area to temporarily avoid the cold and wait for spring to travel west, for the country and for the army, to alleviate the current crisis and pacify the people. Now, according to the original plan, I have ordered them to pack and move on schedule. The opposition still says that my actions are related to Fujian and that there are bad elements in my army, slandering and making groundless accusations, which is heartbreaking to hear. If I were not willing to commit suicide, I would not abandon the country. Seeking perfection only invites destruction, and falsely accusing others misleads the country. I only hope that the Ningxia and Qinghai authorities will understand my plight and allow me to pass through the border. This will not only be a blessing for all officers and soldiers of my army, but also a blessing for the country. But now it is not the case. When my army was traveling, the Ningxia authorities launched a light cavalry attack. My unprepared troops suffered a sudden attack, and we could not avoid it, causing heavy casualties. The Ningxia authorities have spread many rumors and turned against me. Now, they are sending troops from Gansu and Qinghai directly to Ningxia. What is their intention? It is unthinkable. Sir, you are deeply patriotic and have always cared for me. What crime have I committed? I cannot understand. In this difficult situation, I dare to speak frankly. How should I act? I ask for your guidance. Sun Kuiyuan, Ma Yin.

Wang Xiaolai's Reply Telegram

To Commander Sun, please forward from the 41st Army's Office in Nanjing: I have received the Ma telegram. In the Rehe battle, you showed your hard work. After that, in Chahar, you retreated far away. These two battles earned you respect. Later, you were ordered to enter Qinghai, but the large number of troops became a burden, leading to suspicion from neighboring forces. Learning from the past, you should think about how to remedy the situation. I hope that you will strictly abide by the establishment, reduce redundant troops, obey the central government, and withdraw from Ningxia. Then public opinion will consistently be sympathetic, and the country will not be willing to abandon you. The western border is now devastated, and there are repeated alarms from Shule. As a general, you should not meet with military force, which would disrupt the overall situation. Anyone who holds military power and is in a precarious situation is not easy to deal with. Even with Zeng Guofan's qualifications and prestige, when he supervised the Jiangxi army as a vice minister, he was still envied by the governor of Jiangxi. Not to mention others. Therefore, you should not blame others for this, but should seek the solution within yourself. I think it is enough to support your army with the allocated funds, allowing them to be well-fed and well-equipped, and store them for national use. In the past, Kou Xun saw Jia Fu avoid him, and historians did not blame him for his cowardice, but praised him for understanding the overall situation. All these historical precedents can be used as lessons. In recent times, the problem is that there is little friendship between friends who give advice and dissuade from wrongdoing, and much intrigue. This is only enough to mislead you, not to love you. Because I have known you for a long time and cherish the meaning of encouraging soldiers, I dare to offer sincere advice. I hope you will understand. Wang Xiaolai.

The Rice Industry in Northern Shanghai Resumed Operations Yesterday Afternoon After Persuasion

Party and Government Organs Issue Joint Announcement

One Seriously Injured Worker Died from His Injuries

A Post-Mortem Examination Will Be Conducted Today, and a Criminal Lawsuit Will Be Filed

The rice industry laborers and shoulder carriers in Northern Shanghai had a brawl two days ago due to competition for work, injuring 18 people and leading to a strike in the rice industry. Yesterday morning, various businesses continued the strike. In the afternoon, the party and government organs issued a joint announcement persuading them to resume work. A seriously injured worker, Leng Shanlin, died from his injuries yesterday. The Social Bureau ordered the rice industry to review the register of unemployed workers. The rice industry issued an appeal. The details of each item are recorded below.

Continued Strike

More than 30 rice shops, including Wanshengtai, Hengkang, Yutai Xing, Zhicheng, Fengtai, Tongxinggong, Huada, Xinchang, Xiechangde, Suifeng, Wantai Xiang, Yusheng, Dayouheng, Hefengtai, Changfengyi, Ruichangfa, Wanyuanhe, Yuchangxiang, Hengdaxin, Qingshengyi, Dachangrun, Yicheng, Hongchang, Damao, Yongshengtai, Juxingcheng, Rentaisan, and Yudade, Yuanfeng, along the Suzhou River bank near Xinzha Bridge and Wuzhen Road Bridge, continued to strike yesterday morning after shoulder carriers repeatedly caused trouble since the day before.

Joint Announcement

The Social Bureau and the Public Security Bureau issued a joint announcement yesterday stating: "Regarding the conflict between shoulder carriers and rickshaw pullers in the Zhabei rice market, this bureau and the municipal party department have sent personnel to convene both parties for questioning and decided that all existing foremen at the Zhabei rice market docks will be abolished. The rice shops and factories will freely hire foremen, give them fixed wages, and must not extract any fees from the workers' wages, in order to fundamentally improve the situation and eliminate disputes forever. The permit of Shi Dengfu, the head of the shoulder carriers, has been revoked and canceled by this Public Security Bureau. The Municipal Social Bureau has begun to investigate the issue of unemployed workers at the rice market docks and will arrange for the rice shops and factories to provide employment separately. This announcement is hereby issued, ordering all workers to be informed, remain calm, await instructions, and refrain from causing further disturbances. Take heed."

Persuading to Open the Market

Fearing that they would still be obstructed by workers from the Hongshou Yuji shoulder carrying company after opening the market, the rice shops in Northern Shanghai convened an emergency meeting of representatives from various shops at the Shanghai Office of the Soybean and Rice Industry Association on Kulun Road at 11 AM yesterday to discuss how to respond. More than 70 people attended the meeting, which was chaired by Lu Jingwen. After discussion, it was decided to persuade the shops to resume work first. At noon, Jiang Shizhi and Lu Jingwen from the rice industry, along with Tan Kai from the Special Task Force of the Public Security Bureau and Mao, a staff member from the 4th District Public Security Bureau, went door-to-door to persuade the shops to open the market.

Protecting Business Operations

The Public Security Bureau also dispatched more than 30 police officers from the First Squadron of the Police Brigade and 20 armed police officers from the Fourth District Office, together with security guards dispatched by the defense corps, to protect business operations along the river. After the shops opened the market, the rickshaw pullers, fearing that they would be harmed by the shoulder carriers on the way, requested the Public Security Bureau to forward the request to the patrol to protect the rice carts passing by at any time. Fortunately, no incident occurred.

Association Notice

The Shanghai Soybean and Rice Industry Association and the Rice Grain Sales Industry Association issued a joint notice yesterday stating: "We, the undersigned, were forced to suspend business due to the disturbance of the rice market by Shi Dengfu and other workers of the Hongtai Yuji company, and waited for the government to resolve the matter. Now, Mao, a staff member from the Fourth District, and Tan, the captain of the police brigade, have come in person on the orders of Director Wen to earnestly persuade us to resume business and promise to be responsible for protection. Considering that rice is a matter of public concern, and since the Public Security Bureau is responsible for protection, the market should be opened and business resumed. We hope that all fellow merchants will take note."

Death from Injuries

During the fight between rickshaw pullers and shoulder carriers the day before, Leng Shanlin and Xu Songlin were seriously injured. Yesterday, Leng Shanlin died from his serious injuries at the Second Hospital of the Red Cross. (It was also rumored that Xu Songlin died at the same time, but the workers denied it.) The other 16 people who were slightly injured have reported their injuries to the local court and will file a criminal lawsuit based on the law. The court will conduct a post-mortem examination of the deceased today.

Rice Industry Appeal

The Soybean and Rice Industry Association, the Rice Milling Industry Association, and the Rice Grain Sales Industry Association issued an appeal yesterday stating: "It is now reported by various rice shops and rice factories in Northern Shanghai that they have been repeatedly disturbed, intimidated, and threatened by Shi Dengfu and others, interfering with business operations, freely occupying the rice trucks and rickshaws hired by the shops and factories. When their desires are not met, they declare that they will resort to unfavorable means. They have been disrupted several times, resulting in a de facto market shutdown. Now, they are intensifying their actions, creating a dangerous situation. With no other choice, we have to suspend business and await orders. Upon investigation, Shi Dengfu and others, who are the main culprits in disturbing the rice market, falsely established the Hongtai Yuji shoulder carrying company and secretly obtained a license from the Public Security Bureau. Shi Dengfu, claiming to be the head of the shoulder carriers on the Suzhou River, gathered hundreds of unknown people, flaunting and threatening, and surrounding the Xinzha rice market, obstructing rice transportation. Fellow merchants have repeatedly petitioned the municipal party department, the municipal government, the Social Bureau, and the Public Security Bureau, requesting that they be stopped. However, Shi Dengfu and others have been rampant and unlawful, and they have intensified their actions. All fellow merchants have been forced to suspend business, which is indeed the case. We, the undersigned, believe that the country is in serious trouble and that food is important to the people. We have repeatedly endured the disturbances caused by Shi Dengfu and others and have persuaded our fellow merchants to remain calm and wait for the government to resolve the matter. Now, we are in an extremely dangerous situation and unable to protect ourselves. We have no choice but to suspend business and appeal, awaiting the authorities to resolve the matter. We sincerely hope that all sectors, all industries, and all organizations will show sympathy and provide assistance. We are extremely anxious. Sincerely."

One Ship Unloaded in Shanghai

One Ship Transferred to Nanjing

The sixth shipment of wheat purchased from the United States under the loan agreement has arrived from the United States. An Aircraft Crashed in Hongqiao the Day Before Yesterday

A Trainee Named Chen Died on the Spot

Li Jingcong Denies It Was an Eurasia Aircraft

According to the Guowen News Agency, at 1:30 PM the day before yesterday, an aircraft crashed in Hongqiao, killing a trainee named Chen. At the time, there were four trainees being instructed by foreigners on the field. It was said that trainee Chen took off first and had just reached about 120 feet in the air when the engine suddenly stalled, and the aircraft fell to the ground with the person. Chen died on the spot, and the aircraft was completely destroyed. A steel pillar on the aircraft penetrated Chen's chest and abdomen. The flying helmet he was wearing could not be removed due to the brain matter splattering out. As for which organization the aircraft belonged to, the reporter inquired at the Eurasia Company yesterday. He met with Li Jingcong, the manager of the company, who said that he knew nothing about this incident and that it was probably an aircraft from other military organizations. When the reporter inquired about which military organization it belonged to, he said that he did not know, so there was no way to find out the details. It was later learned that the name of the so-called trainee Chen was only known in Western characters as C.C. Chen. The central government and his family have been notified, and the central government has provided 5,000 yuan in compensation to handle his funeral.

International Wireless Telegraph Bureau

Yesterday's Reception for the Press

Director Wen Reported at the Dinner

Resolving Problems Inappropriately in Guangdong

Yesterday's Supplementary Treaty Signed Regarding the Wusong Ship Case

Settled by the Seamen's Preparatory Committee and Butterfield & Swire Company

The Chinese Version of the Agreement is the Legal Basis for Both Parties

The Seven Articles are Comprehensive and Satisfactory in Content

The tragic case of the Butterfield & Swire Company's Wusong ship, in which workers were dismissed and injured, has dragged on for almost a year. Although a resolution was announced in Guangzhou last November, the contents of the agreement were riddled with errors and were unsatisfactory to the workers. The most heartbreaking and disappointing aspects were: first, the number of workers to be reinstated was not clearly specified; second, non-reinstated workers would only receive a subsidy of 25 yuan each; third, no worker representatives participated in the signing of the agreement; and fourth, the recall registration process, awaiting reorganization, disregarded the union's position and the workers' welfare. After a year of heavy sacrifice, such an outcome not only ignored the interests of the workers but also set a bad precedent, damaging the long-term labor movement and national vitality, and playing into the hands of imperialism. Upon hearing this, people from all walks of life were indignant, especially the workers on the ship who were directly affected. They appealed to the Chinese Seamen's Union Preparatory Committee to uphold justice and resolve this dire situation. The committee also considered the handling of the case in Guangzhou to be inappropriate and shared the same indignation. Based on the workers' request and their own sense of duty, the committee dispatched secretaries Hou Dachun and Sun Lupi in early December to strongly argue with the company. However, Butterfield & Swire adopted a tough stance, initially refusing to negotiate, then claiming that the matter had already been resolved by a seamen's organization in Guangzhou, and finally resorting to threats, expressing their willingness to suspend shipping operations. Nevertheless, the union's determination remained firm, vowing not to rest until the goal of improvement was achieved. The key points raised by the union for correction included: (1) specifying the number of workers to be reinstated as 35 to 40; (2) increasing the subsidy for non-reinstated workers to 30 yuan; (3) resolving the problem of reorganizing the middle-class crew should involve the union's participation; and (4) recognizing the union's right to recommend and oversee dismissals, etc. For two months, secretaries Hou and Sun, disregarding all obstacles and difficulties, bravely moved forward, continuing to negotiate with Butterfield & Swire more than a dozen times, appealing to reason and pointing out the benefits and drawbacks. Their painstaking efforts were admirable. Only in recent days did the company gradually concede. Finally, the day before yesterday, the two sides' opinions had approached, and it was decided to supplement the existing conditions. Butterfield & Swire not only accepted all the points raised by the union headquarters but also expressed sincere admiration for the union's spirit of serving the public good. At the same time, out of respect for China's national dignity, they agreed to use the Chinese version of the treaty as the legal basis, which is rarely seen when signing treaties with foreigners. This supplementary treaty was signed at Butterfield & Swire at 4 p.m. yesterday. The union convened an emergency meeting in the morning and appointed Zhang Jianbai as the signing representative and Sun Lupi as the witness. On the worker side, Wang Oumin was appointed as the witness and Jiang Genggui as the representative. The company was represented by White and witnessed by Yuan Lupi. With this, the dispute was fundamentally resolved. All workers who should be reinstated reportedly boarded the ship last night. The various treaty provisions are recorded below:

Treaty Signed in Guangzhou

(1) If Butterfield & Swire can prove the survival and well-being of the missing worker Gao Kunquan, the issue of compensation will be waived. This evidence must be submitted to the witness within two weeks. (2) Butterfield & Swire will recall all 126 dismissed stewards from the Wusong ship from the date of signing, register them in the worker roster, and pay them salaries as before, with the same terms as the original workers, within one month. Butterfield & Swire will reorganize the stewards on the Wusong ship. After the reorganization, in addition to those who remain on the ship, each surplus worker will be paid a subsidy of 25 yuan. (3) All workers on the Guangzhou-Foshan ship, as well as the coolies, stevedores and workers on all small vessels at the Butterfield & Swire warehouse in Guangzhou, will be reinstated as before. (4) After the signing of these conditions, Butterfield & Swire agrees to restore the previous favorable treatment to worker merchants, and the Seamen's Union agrees to cancel the strike. The Guangzhou Chamber of Commerce agrees to persuade merchants to resume trading with Butterfield & Swire and will no longer demand compensation for all losses incurred during the strike period.

Yesterday's Supplementary Treaty

Regarding the Wusong ship dispute, Butterfield & Swire is willing to sign a supplementary treaty with the Chinese Seamen's Union Preparatory Committee (hereinafter referred to as the Seamen's Union) as follows: (1) Articles 1, 3, and 4 of the original treaty signed in Guangdong will be maintained. (2) Article 2 of the original treaty signed in Guangdong is supplemented as follows: (a) The number of original Wusong ship workers remaining on the ship is fixed at 35 to 40. (b) The subsidy for each surplus worker, except those remaining on the ship, is changed to 30 yuan. This amount will be paid by the company to the union for distribution. (c) Non-reinstated workers should be given priority when the company's ships need workers. (3) The issue of reorganizing the entire middle-class crew will be resolved through long-term consultation between the Shanghai Shipping Trade Association and the Seamen's Union. (4) Butterfield & Swire agrees that there will be no more instances of armed eviction of workers. (5) Butterfield & Swire agrees to consider accepting workers recommended by the Seamen's Union and agrees not to dismiss workers without legitimate reasons. (6) This treaty is based on the Chinese text. (7) This treaty shall take effect from the date of signing. Furthermore, it is reported that the workers are now very happy with the swift resolution and the satisfactory content of the treaty and will petition the Preparatory Committee to hold a general meeting on a regular basis to celebrate.

The Yellow River is in Flood

The Hebei Yellow River Disaster Relief Association Pleads for Emergency Relief

More than 100 Villages in Two Districts Have Been Completely Submerged

Disaster Victims are Without Food or Clothing, Their Cries Fill the Wilderness

The Shanghai Joint Association for Raising Emergency Relief for the Yellow River Flood, received a letter yesterday from the Hebei Provincial Yellow River Flood Relief Committee, stating that a sudden thaw had caused a catastrophic flood in Changyuan County in the province. Successive reports from the county government and the Bureau of Public Works indicated the disaster was severe, and they pleaded for a quick allocation of funds to provide relief and save the people. The original letter and telegrams are recorded below:

Letter from the Yellow River Disaster Relief Association

Respected Sirs: We have recently received successive telegrams from Changyuan County Magistrate Bu Hengxun, Investigation Committee members Zhang Qin and Yang Shulin, and Yellow River Conservancy Bureau Director Sun Qingze, reporting that a sudden thaw in Changyuan County in this province has caused a steep rise in the water level. Ice floes were carried out of the breach and flooded over one hundred villages in the second and fifth districts of the county. The water depth on the plains is three to four feet, and everything has been submerged. The old and young have drowned, their bodies lying everywhere. Those who escaped are without food or clothing, their cries fill the wilderness, a truly unbearable scene. We earnestly request a quick allocation of emergency relief to save the victims. Accordingly, we have learned that the recent flooding in Changyuan County in this province, caused by the Yellow River's rising water and sudden thaw, has caused the victims to suffer great hardship. In this severe winter, the suffering is truly unprecedented. In addition to sending members of this association to distribute emergency relief and telegraphing the central headquarters and the Disaster Relief Group for investigation and relief efforts, the matter concerns saving lives, and we have always admired your association's great concern for the disaster situation in this province. We are sending you a copy of the original telegrams and request that you investigate and provide generous assistance and relief efforts, for which we will be eternally grateful.

Telegram from Changyuan County

To the Hebei Provincial Government Yellow River Flood Relief Committee in Tianjin: The water disaster in Changyuan this time is most tragic. We are deeply grateful for your repeated dispatch of personnel to provide relief and assistance to the people. Unexpectedly, while the investigation and relief efforts were underway, a sudden surge of ice floes occurred on January 13th, causing the water level to rise sharply, completely submerging over one hundred villages in the second and fifth districts. The water depth on the plains is varying from three to five feet. With the harshness of the severe winter, the old and young drowned, their bodies lying everywhere. The young and strong who escaped were without food or clothing, their cries filling the wilderness, a truly unbearable scene. Those who have come to the city in search of a meal or a place to live number in the hundreds. It has not been long, but more and more are coming. Those who linger on the east bank of the river, crying and wailing on the levee, are countless. The cause of this ice floe flood is that the breach at Shitou Village has not been blocked. Downstream from Shitou Village to Gaoping in Hua County, the water is scattered and shallow, the riverbed is unstable, and the flow is slow. It has completely frozen over. The sudden rush from above was blocked, leading to widespread flooding without any end in sight. In short, if the breach is not blocked for a day, the victims will not have a way out for a day. If this period is delayed any further, the people will sink further into misery and decline, and who knows what the consequences will be. In addition to the county quickly taking measures to provide relief, we are sending this telegram to report and hope that you will quickly send emergency relief to save the flood victims who have been repeatedly affected in this area, and urge you to quickly block the breach to prevent future disasters. We would be most grateful. Signed, Acting Changyuan County Magistrate Bu Hengxun, Acting Secretary Pang Yuanshu, Investigation Committee Members Zhang Qin and Yang Shulin, Yellow River Flood Relief Committee Deputy Chairman Sun Tingrui.

Telegram from the Bureau of Public Works

To the Hebei Provincial Disaster Relief Committee: The ice flood has risen one meter in the past two days. Outside the main dyke, the water has already reached the dyke roots. The villages have once again been submerged in deep water. Piles of ice floes are being carried wildly by the currents. There are few boats and the roads are blocked, making escape impossible. The victims will either die in the water or freeze to death. The treetops and rooftops are converging towards the dyke. There is no way to provide rescue. We have seen the village walls of Tielu Village surrounded by water. The terrain inside the village is higher than outside by over ten feet, but even though we are trying to block the water, we fear we cannot protect it to the end. The situation is dire. The victims are kneeling on the dyke, crying and begging for help, unable to speak. The scene is extremely tragic. In addition to requesting the Industry and Relief Group to detain the large boats at the breach and quickly release them into the disaster area, we have also sent personnel to the disaster area overnight to provide relief. However, the accumulation of ice floes makes travel difficult, and the flood area is wide. Please send a special commissioner to rescue the remaining people as soon as possible, and please send the original telegram to the newspapers, asking them to join forces in appealing. We are anxiously awaiting orders with tears and urgency. Signed, Member Sun Qingze, bowing.

The Trade Bureau Prepares

Opinions on the Export of Cattle and Beef

Establishing Farmers' Loan Offices to Develop Animal Husbandry

Inviting Experts to Guide Farmers in Improving Animal Husbandry

The International Trade Bureau previously received a letter from the Commercial Department of the Ministry of Industry, requesting an investigation into the export of cattle and beef from our country and the preparation of opinions. Director He immediately ordered the Guidance Department to conduct an investigation and prepare a plan after receiving the letter. It is understood that the Guidance Department has prepared a plan and sent a letter to the Commercial Department for reference. The opinions on the export of cattle and beef are as follows:

Loans to Farmers

(1) In recent years, the rural areas have been depressed, and farmers lack capital. If they borrow money from private individuals, the interest rates are too high, and the cost of raising cattle is relatively large. If they do not have enough ability, it will be difficult to raise cattle. To make rural finance active, local officials should allocate funds, or local wealthy people should raise funds to establish farmers' loan offices, lending to farmers at low interest rates, to be repaid when they produce. This will give farmers capital and enable them to develop animal husbandry and increase production.

Preventing Cattle Diseases

(2) There is a lack of veterinarians in the countryside. If there is cattle plague or other diseases, farmers can only sit and wait for death. The cost of raising cattle is large, and the life and death of cattle is of great importance to farmers. Therefore, to prevent cattle diseases, local government offices must send veterinarians to the cattle-raising areas for inspection, or establish small-scale veterinary hospitals to diagnose and treat cattle diseases, in order to develop animal husbandry.

Organizing Cooperatives

(3) Cattle are traded by cattle merchants who buy from farmers and resell to cattle markets, and then the cattle markets resell to exporters. This indirect trade involves several transfers from the cattle raiser to the exporter, and the middleman's exploitation is high. Moreover, cattle merchants often monopolize prices, and cattle merchants deliberately suppress prices to make profits, causing farmers to suffer a great loss. To avoid unfair trading, local government offices can convene cattle-raising farmers to organize sales cooperatives for joint sales, which is both convenient and economical.

Improving Animal Husbandry

(4) Our country's animal husbandry methods are outdated and do not know how to improve. There is no research on cattle feed and cattle barns. As a result, countless lean and sick cattle die. Local government offices should hire experts to guide farmers to improve animal husbandry using scientific methods, so as to ensure that vegetable cattle are fat and plowing cattle are strong, in order to increase cattle production. (5) In recent years, there have been more and more ranches in various places, but there are too few animal husbandry talents and veterinarians. In the future, schools should be established to train specialized talents in this field in order to improve and develop animal husbandry.
