Judging from the current Shanghai market, although the price has risen by more than 10 yuan, it is still difficult to make a profit. Yesterday's market price for ordinary high-grade wood ear was 80 yuan to 78 yuan, and it looked tighter afterwards.

Silk, Tea, and Foreign Exchange Depreciation Affect Silk Sales

(China Silk Transported to the United States Has Become Scarce) The United States has always been the largest consumer of China silk. In the most prosperous period, 4,000 to 5,000 bales were shipped to the United States every month. In recent years, due to the encroachment of Japanese silk and rayon, the sales of China silk to the United States have declined sharply. The quantity of China silk shipped from Shanghai to the United States last month (i.e., January) has become scarce. Only 295 bales were shipped in the entire month, all of which were white factory silk. The other yellow, white, and gray silk were not shipped to the United States.

(Duplex Silk Supply Cannot Meet Demand) Recently, the spring sales of duplex silk have started, and the demand from India is increasing. However, only Fulun silk factory in Shanghai is working, and the silk production is not abundant, so the supply cannot meet the demand. Last month (i.e., January), a total of 228 bales of duplex silk were shipped to India.

(Foreign Firms are Waiting for the Right Time) The overseas raw silk market, because the sales season has arrived, the current silk market price is becoming increasingly firm. Although New York and Lyon sent telegrams yesterday morning to inquire about the market price of yellow and white factory silk, the foreign exchange continued to depreciate, so the Chinese silk merchants are still waiting for the right time because the prices do not match. Yesterday, only Xinfu imported 20 bales of white factory silk and Zhonghe imported 20 bales of gray silk, and the price rose by 5-6 yuan.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

A Wealthy Man Despises Money

— Liu

In ancient China, there was a scholar who so detested money that he refused to call it money, instead referring to it as "Aduwu" (a derogatory term for money). He hated this thing to the point of disliking even its name. However, this scholar was not wealthy. His aversion to money likely stemmed from a lack of it, and from being oppressed by it. In today's money-driven society, this is not surprising. A news report from Athens, Greece, tells of a very wealthy industrialist named Ramas who displayed a peculiar eccentricity. From the top of his residence, he scattered banknotes of 100, 500, and 1000 drachmas (the Greek currency). Passersby scrambled to grab them. In a world plagued by economic panic, where the rich get richer and the poor get poorer, the poor may outwardly despise money, but their eyes light up at the sight of it. It is no wonder that thousands of Athens' poor, hearing of the wealthy man scattering banknotes, gathered spontaneously to compete for the airborne currency, to the point where "the scramble devolved into a riot."

A wealthy man becomes wealthy by desperately seizing money. But now, this foreign wealthy man says he deeply loathes this filthy lucre and feels burdened and wearied by it. This reveals that money is capable of inspiring loathing in both the poor and the rich. Consider that in ancient times, trade was conducted solely through barter. Later, someone invented the ingenious method of using currency as a medium of exchange. Since then, although humans were meant to use this treasure, the treasure has instead used humans. The inventor of this system is truly detestable. Our historical records and mythological legends credit Suirenshi with the discovery of fire, Shennongshi with the discovery of medicine, and the Yellow Emperor with the invention of the navigational compass. However, no explicit record exists of the inventor of currency. Perhaps "the originator of a practice without funeral statuettes will have no descendants." His name has vanished, and his fame remains unproclaimed. The reason for the currency inventor's nameless obscurity is that the ancients also deeply detested money, unwilling to propagate his great name to future generations in the same way they celebrated the virtues of Suirenshi and Shennongshi.

During the Spring and Autumn period, Confucius said, "If wealth could be obtained by seeking it, I would become a mere whip-holder." This shows that wealthy people already existed at that time, and they were already powerful figures. Therefore, although Confucius did not desire wealth, he still taught Zigong the ways of commerce. However, even a sage like Confucius only refrained from seeking wealth and did not deeply loathe money. This shows that even sages are powerless against the magic of money. Now, this foreign wealthy man in Greece has come to despise money. Is he more accomplished than our Chinese sages?

The news report states that police, deeming him "mentally deranged, sent him to a certain hospital." In a capitalist society, to uphold the dignity of the capitalist system, labeling him "mentally deranged" is naturally the best approach. However, it is regrettable that we can no longer hear the opinions of this wealthy man who rejects money.

In Shanghai, we have not heard of wealthy people despising money. In fact, once someone becomes wealthy, they face the risk of being kidnapped and extorted by bandits, restricted in their freedom, and constantly filled with anxiety. Clearly, they are burdened by money. How can they willingly endure this? Perhaps this is why the monetary system is so remarkably great. However, in the eyes of the poor, this monetary system is the source and control center of all social evils. Everyone curses it, everyone deeply loathes it. This is why society is not peaceful. If all the wealthy people in the world despised money, the world would certainly be at peace. I believe this to be true.

Rent Reduction Movement

— Guang Han

Recently, various groups in this city, due to the post-Songhu Battle situation, have seen increasing economic depression. However, instead of rents being reduced, some have even increased. Therefore, they are demanding lower rents to ease the burden and revitalize the prosperity of the city. A committee has been formed to carry out a rent reduction movement, which is something worthy of our attention.

Among life's necessities, besides clothing and food, housing is undoubtedly essential. Shanghai is a major trading port in our country, with a population of over three million. The housing issue has become a serious problem in society. The high cost of Shanghai's rent has always been the highest in the country, and property owners only think of their own benefit, ignoring the livelihood of the people. They often raise rents, causing countless residents to lose most of their annual income to landlords. The impact on individuals' livelihoods is obvious, and the market will decline, leading to social unrest. The only solution is rent reduction. Therefore, the rent reduction movement is a legitimate action to solve residents' housing problems. Solving housing problems can not only allow individuals to live in peace and prosperity but also promote the prosperity of the market and maintain social tranquility. However, while expressing our full support for the movement, we cannot help but notice a major flaw. It seems that the committee's efforts are only focused on representing businesses and secondary landlords in demanding rent reduction from primary landlords, while ignoring the sub-tenants. This can be seen from the committee's resolutions. Here, we must ask: Among the residents who rent houses, besides businesses and secondary landlords, aren't there also sub-tenants? Although there are no statistics on the number of sub-tenants in the city, it can be said that they are numerous. Moreover, secondary landlords often pass on the pressure from primary landlords to sub-tenants. The suffering of sub-tenants is no less than that of secondary landlords. Now that secondary landlords are unwilling to endure the exploitation of primary landlords and are demanding rent reduction, it is dictated by the situation. Don't sub-tenants also have sufficient reason to resist the exploitation of secondary landlords? Therefore, I believe that if the committee only represents the interests of secondary landlords, then this movement is not thorough and will not have much impact on the entire population. Perhaps some may say that if the primary landlord reduces the rent, not only will the secondary landlord directly benefit, but the sub-tenant will also indirectly benefit. Once the goal of the secondary landlord is achieved, the rent for the sub-tenant can naturally be reduced. I think this is not necessarily the case. It must be understood that human nature is selfish. Although secondary landlords feel the pain themselves and appeal to primary landlords, they may not necessarily sympathize with the situation of sub-tenants or be willing to concede. Therefore, I believe that if people in society truly want to alleviate the people's difficulties, revitalize the market, and maintain society, this rent reduction movement must be thorough and universal. Not only should demands for rent reduction be made to primary landlords, but also the same advice should be given to secondary landlords. Only in this way will it benefit the majority of Shanghai residents, and only then can it help the prosperity of the market and the tranquility of society!

Confession of an Ideal Life

— Wen Bing

Whenever people mention living life, it seems as if one must sharpen their heads and squeeze into this turbid society. However, I hate this argument the most. I always feel that this is a display of servility, a most profound exposure of the base behavior of people. Why must living life involve being obsequious? Why must living life involve relying on the whims of those corrupt individuals and living a precarious existence? I do not understand this deviation from human nature. I do not understand why they must squeeze into this so-called professional society, pushing each other out, engaging in cutthroat competition, knocking others down while they rush forward to take their place? Why must they be so base? If human life must be colored by such base behavior, then why don't they just die?

As for me, I am rebelling against them. I cannot have such intentions. If I were to have such intentions, then I would no longer be myself. I would already be one of them.

As for me, although I feel the same way that I have to live since I was born, I do not have the same opinions on how to live as they do; if I were to live a life of servility, relying on the whims of others, then I would rather die sooner. Because so-called life must have a noble meaning, a vibrant sense of life, which can never be expressed in such servility.

How shall I choose my way of life? I am determined to do it this way: I will decide to live the life of a recluse like the sages of the past. I would rather be indifferent and live in seclusion among the mountains and valleys, unknown to the world. I will not visit any great men, nor will I be close to any powerful figures. Let nature always be pure and sacred to me, let the bright moon be my companion, and let the clear spring reflect my heart! Let the sanctions of society and the shackles of society forever leave me.

From this quiet life, let me immerse myself in the poetic spirit of those ancient poets, and let my heart, untainted by worldliness, forever be with those great and sacred hearts. As for the world, I am willing to abandon it to those worldly people, let them meet each other with bombs and pistols in their meetings! Let them betray friends and relatives betray relatives!……

Perhaps some may scold me for speaking nonsense, but that is where they are wrong! In this turbid and inaccessible society, being able to pull oneself out of all disputes, not only not watching arrogantly from the sidelines but also suddenly going into seclusion, this cannot but be said to be another kind of natural state of mind! Is it that even this, not disturbing others at all, not interfering in other people's lives at all, is not allowed by the world? If even this is not allowed, then this is truly a tyrannical world! "What else can be said!"

The Inevitability of the Commodification of Love

— Lie Huo

People in general (perhaps including myself) often bitterly denounce the fact that modern women's love has been trampled on by money and has simply become a commodity. While this is true, it is actually inevitable. What in this world is not trampled on by money? What is there that has not become a commodity? In Sinclair's "The Jungle," there was such a description of the situation in the slaughterhouse. He said that because the organization of the machines was so strict, no matter whether it was beef, cowhide, cow bones, or cow hair, not even half a bit would be wasted. Even cow blood and cow dung each had its own use; the only thing that could not be made into a commodity was the miserable cry of the cow being slaughtered. This is of course a sharp description, and also a true description, because the spirit of modern society is just like that.

If we know that in modern society not only has physical labor become a commodity, but even intellectual labor has also become a commodity, then we will not be surprised that modern society has made love into a commodity. Workers need to live, so they sell their labor. Intellectuals such as scholars, professors, philosophers, writers, artists, scientists, etc., in order to live, sell their knowledge, writings, works of art, and new inventions. And when a woman wants to make herself survive, and when she has nothing better than her body and her love to sell, she can only sell her only body and love to the buyer. The reason for this is the problem of survival. If a person can appreciate the fervent desire to survive, then he will not be surprised by this kind of selling of one's most precious things for survival. It is originally difficult for a modern woman to make a living. If we pay attention to their talents, their physical constitutions, and their positions, we will be able to understand this point. Even if they stand on an equal footing with men, it is difficult to defeat men, let alone when they are in a position different from men? We know that all people want to survive, and women are of course no exception. But what do they rely on to survive? This is the biggest reason why they sell their love. They are moving and flirtatious, and these two major elements of being moving and flirtatious constitute the main components of their becoming commodities. In addition, they are particularly fond of vanity, and the expression of vanity is all kinds of things that can only be bought with a lot of money. Therefore, their natural buyers are of course those who are rich and can often buy these noble things to satisfy their vanity.

Generally speaking, only moving appearance, youthful handsomeness, and a kind of warm and enthusiastic mood are the elements that arouse love in women. Originally this is correct. However, these things are not ultimately money. In their minds, even if it is a very handsome and lovable young man, it would be a very painful thing if he could only settle his lover in a low and foul-smelling shack. Therefore, in our view, vanity seems to be unimportant, but women cannot think this way. In feudal society, the height of a person was expressed by their rank. At that time, there were nobles who were so poor that they did not have a penny to their name who were respected. There were facts of nobles wearing torn noble clothes at high-class banquets. This kind of being respected even when they were so poor that they did not have a penny and were wearing torn clothes was a unique characteristic of the feudal system. Looking back, when we see the current capitalist society, the fact that people are respected if they have money is of course the same inevitable phenomenon. What can a person resist about their environment? If her environment wants her to do this. So I feel that we don't need to curse them either, because they are originally so weak and pitiful.

However, it is not that I have not taken into account the problem of these young people who take love as bread, but I feel that this problem cannot be mixed up with cursing them. Of course, love becoming a commodity is a bad thing, and I also feel that this bad thing is even worse for our ordinary young people. However, I always feel that this is not a problem of social sanctions, nor a problem of education, nor even a problem of curses. This problem is directly related to the existence of current society! Thinking of solving this problem from the point of social sanctions will definitely not be effective. Because in this current society, who can impose their sanctions? In other words, wanting to eliminate it from the point of view of education will not have any success either. Because in this current society, education has fundamentally lost its dominance. If it comes to cursing, that fundamentally cannot solve anything, but only disturbs oneself in vain for a while.

If we want to make love not become a commodity, then... forgive me for stopping speaking and putting down my pen here. || The End ||

The Outrageous Act of an Athenian Millionaire

— Mu Lang

According to a news report from Athens the other day:

A millionaire and major industrialist here named Mr. Lai Ma had a peculiar fit of eccentricity today. From the top of his residence, he scattered banknotes of one hundred, five hundred, and one thousand drachmas (the name of the Greek currency) downwards, causing passersby to scramble to grab them. This news instantly spread throughout the city, and tens of thousands of people gathered spontaneously, scrambling to grab the banknotes flying in the air. By the time the police arrived to suppress the situation, the scrambling had turned into a riot. They had no choice but to mobilize reserve soldiers to disperse the crowd. Later, the police entered Mr. Lai Ma's residence again and forbade him from throwing banknotes down again. However, when Mr. Lai saw the police enter his room, he immediately tore up the banknotes piled up like a mountain in front of him; and told the police: he deeply hated this kind of filthy money and said that he was deeply burdened by this "Adu thing" and felt quite pressured and tired. The police, thinking that he was mentally deranged, sent him to a certain hospital. His family checked his accounts and found that he had scattered more than one hundred thousand drachmas in an instant.

This shocking news, along with its power of dissemination, shook the hearts of every money-obsessed person in the world. We can imagine how enthusiastic and chaotic the state of the crowd under the house scrambling madly when the millionaire Mr. Lai Ma was scattering his banknotes? I cannot be sure exactly to what extent that enthusiastic state had reached, but I think the hopeful expressions of the general men, women, old and young who were craning their necks in the street a few years ago when a certain tobacco company scattered leaflets from an airplane in Shanghai that could be exchanged for cigarettes may be able to imagine one ten-thousandth of the madness of the crowd under the Athenian millionaire's house now.

However, apart from the description of the crowd, what deserves our attention is the hysterical behavior of that millionaire. Not being a psychologist, I cannot determine whether that millionaire belongs to a type of abnormality, but at least his nervous system suddenly lacked order, which is beyond doubt. One often hears people say that if one does too much of other things, one feels disgusted, such as feeling nauseous from eating too much food, or getting sleep sickness from sleeping too much. Only money is such a thing that no one ever complains about having too much of it, no matter what. But now it is not so. Now there are also people who hate money, no, not only hate it, but even tear up the banknotes that represent money. Isn't this contrary to the normal state of evolution? Granted, on the surface, Mr. Lai Ma's distributing banknotes to the crowd is a rare act of kindness or grandeur, but if we examine the reality, is he really bestowing blessings on all living beings? This can be known by just looking at his conversation with the police: he deeply hated this kind of filthy money... so it can be known that it is definitely not. He also said, "Deeply burdened by this 'Adu thing,' I feel quite pressured and tired." Therefore, his "deep hatred" of money is precisely a reaction to his past excessive "greed for money as if it were his life." From the Buddhist theory, this is the cycle of cause and effect. There is a famous saying in our ancient Chinese books, "Greed makes one lose one's mind," which can also be a portrayal of Mr. Lai Ma.

In China, I have never heard of such news, so a "fool" like Mr. Lai Ma is definitely hard to find in China. However, from daily life, we can often experience the same painful feelings as Mr. Lai Ma, but our opportunities are relatively small or indifferent, so our feelings are not so profound.

For example, someone bought an airline lottery ticket one day, and from that day until the lottery day, he almost lost sleep every night. When he knew that the number he bought was not the winning one after the lottery, he was relieved instead. In these dozens or days of anxious thought, he must have lost a few pounds of weight. If he won the grand prize, what a more severe and difficult test would this be for his mental and physical strength! Perhaps my words are a bit exaggerated, but I still feel that it is said of the general object.

However, those who suffer never complain about the bestower of the suffering they have suffered. Perhaps they do not even know who is causing their suffering, and of course, there is no way to complain. A millionaire may not be impossible to be, and wealth may not be impossible to accumulate, but if one becomes a millionaire and has money, but is instead subject to spiritual restraint or torment, then is wealth a happiness for people, or is it just suffering many pains in vain, and not even making a fortune, but suffering many pains in vain, like those who buy lottery tickets!

Here, the Athenian millionaire found an object to vent his pain - tearing up the banknotes - which is a clever and worthy prescription to imitate, because at least he can be free from worries from now on.

A Secret to Getting Along in the World

— Xue Fei

In the past, those who paid attention to getting along in the world generally did nothing more than the following two things: one was flattering, and the other was bragging. This is a well-known fact. Recently, I have developed a new secret to getting along in the world. This is to treat everyone as a bad person first. Don't easily express what's in your heart to anyone. Don't casually believe what others say. That is to say, always be three parts hypocritical to everyone.

Originally, hypocrisy can also be classified as part of bragging, but here it is necessary to specifically discuss and study it. Why? Because this is a secret to getting along in the world that ordinary people do not pay much attention to. And I especially suffered great practical harm because I did not understand this secret to getting along in the world, so I have a special understanding of this secret. I am qualified to talk about this issue.

The reason why I did not understand this secret and suffered practical harm is because I excessively believed the many honest words spoken by a friend, and as a result, I was betrayed by this friend. From this experience, I realized that one cannot be too honest when speaking. Being honest will make one "die unjustly," as Shanghai people say. Originally, this is something that people with some experience know. The reason why I was betrayed by a friend is not some unexpected encounter. It is a common thing in society, but I didn't even know it. Not only did I not know, but I am afraid that many young people in society are as confused as I am. This is a personal matter and not worth mentioning, so let's talk about things on a larger scale in society. Which thing in society is real? We know that advertisements in newspapers fundamentally have no reason to be believed. Their words must be at least × discounted. However, so-called news is also based on the principle of "recording everything heard." Only heaven and earth know what was actually heard.

So, is the entire society fundamentally unreal? That is not the case either. From another point of view, everything in society is real. How can this be explained? This must be seen horizontally from the combination of interests and vertically from the succession and evolution of interests before and after. We know that the combination of society is fundamentally a combination of interests; and the evolution of society is the succession and change of these interests. Recognizing this point, then we can grasp the center of the facts. If you can figure out the relationship of interests between them, then there is nothing that is not very simple. That is, everything comes naked with only interests. What morality... is nothing more than deceiving people. Thoroughly speaking, so-called morality and friendship are fundamentally built on the basis of interests. Without interests, there is no so-called morality and friendship. It was like this in ancient times, and it is even more so in modern times. If you want to abandon the relationship of interests and seek from other aspects, then you will be clueless about everything, and you will only feel that neither left nor right is right.

Since everything in the world is only true with regard to interests, then our secret to getting along in the world can be known. This is that you can only find your true friends in the relationship of interests. When he is good to you, he is definitely not truly loving you, but rather making use of you; when he no longer needs you, he may as well kick you away. If you think that he is sincerely treating you well, because you sincerely treat him, then you are making a big mistake, and as a result, you will definitely be fooled by him. This is an essential secret to getting along in the world.

Fiction

The Lonely Person (3)

— Dai Ni

(II) On the Shanghai-Hangzhou Road

Immediately, Kejia helped Xiaoxun pack his luggage. The so-called luggage was very simple: a few changes of clothes, daily necessities, and books. After everything was packed, Kejia said: "I only came to Hangzhou the day before yesterday and saw you twice. The old nanny said you hadn't returned for two days. Staying at home, I'm afraid Grandma would say I'm still running around even when I'm getting married, so I stayed at the Lakeside Hotel. Since we're leaving tomorrow, I'll settle the room bill, and we'll sleep in the same bed tonight, how about that?"

"Okay! Isn't there any more lecturing to do?" Xiaoxun said with a laugh. He returned to his writing chair, crossed his legs, and habitually took out two cigarettes from the tobacco jar, handing one to Kejia, saying, "Let's smoke cigarettes instead."

Yeniu twitched the corner of his mouth, swallowing the words he was about to say. The two lit their cigarettes, and he went out.

Xiaoxun smoothed his naturally loose and curly hair, and the white smoke he exhaled, accompanied by the spring breeze, scattered outside the window in various ways. Indeed, that night, they talked about everything. They talked about Xiaoxun's romance with Qinbo, whether "being lovelorn is painful," and whether Kejia and Jingyi's "game" was embellishing life, all the sorrows falling behind the joys. The sky had unknowingly begun the next day. Xiaoxun called the old nanny to get up, and after washing up, they rushed to catch the early train to Shanghai. Although Xiaoxun said he was recuperating, this was the first time he had gotten up so early since coming to the West Lake.

Looking into the distance, the sun emerged from the mountain hollow, and its golden light shone on the lake surface. The March spring breeze blew, and the surface of the water rippled with the reflection of the willow branches, like ten thousand golden snakes swimming up from the clear water. Xiaoxun raised his naturally loose and curly hair, gently exhaled, and muttered to himself in the rickshaw: "I recognize the beauty of West Lake today."

The rickshaw puller slapped his thighs and quickly reached the train station in the morning breeze. Xiaoxun nervously glanced at the entire Hangzhou station, as if he were parting from his newlywed wife. Although he detested the ordinariness of life, he couldn't help but fall in love with it after staying for three months. "Contradictory life!" Kejia saw through Xiaoxun's feelings and smiled like he was singing a hymn.

They boarded the train amidst the noisy crowd, and with a whistle, the train slowly started moving. The two did not speak. Two different trains of thought occupied each other's minds. Their bodies felt a harmonious rhythm with the comfortable cushions, and in this peaceful environment, they were lulled into a hazy slumber.

The fields and houses on both sides receded backward, and a long train roared forward. When it stopped at Jiaxing Station, they were awakened by a woman's shout. Xiaoxun raised his head and saw a woman on the opposite seat looking at him with a friendly smile, thinking that the woman was laughing at them for sleeping soundly, he pretended to look out at the platform, feeling embarrassed. Kejia raised his eyelids slightly, then lowered his head again. Seeing that he hadn't noticed her, the woman moved closer to the small table separating the two seats, and tilted her head to say: "Kejia, we've arrived in Shanghai."
